–ü—Ä–æ–ª–æ–≥: –ó–≤—É–∫–∏ –¥–æ–∂–¥—è ‚Äã

–ö–∞–ø–ª—è –∑–∞ –∫–∞–ø–ª–µ–π.





–∫–∞–ø–ª—è –∑–∞ –∫–∞–ø–ª–µ–π, –∫–∞–ø–ª—è –∑–∞ –∫–∞–ø–ª–µ–π‚Ä¶





–≠—Ç–æ—Ç –≥–æ—Ä–æ–¥ —É—Ç–æ–Ω—É–ª –≤ —Ä–∏—Ç–º–µ –∫–∞–ø–µ–ª—å..





–î–æ–∂–¥—å —É—Å–∏–ª–∏–≤–∞–µ—Ç—Å—è.





–Ø —Å—Ç–æ—é –ø–æ–¥ –∫–∞—Ä–Ω–∏–∑–æ–º –ª–µ—Å—Ç–Ω–∏—á–Ω–æ–π –∫–ª–µ—Ç–∫–∏ –Ω–∞ –∫—Ä—ã—à–µ, –±–µ—Å—á–∏—Å–ª–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–µ –∫–∞–ø–ª–∏ –ø–∞–¥–∞—é—â–∏–µ –Ω–∞ –∑–µ–º–ª—é, —Å–æ–∑–¥–∞—é—â–∏–µ –ø—É–ª—å—Å–∞—Ü–∏–∏, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä–∞—è –∫–∞–∂–µ—Ç—Å—è –∫–∞–∫ –æ—Ä–∫–µ—Å—Ç—Ä –≤–µ—á–Ω–æ–π —Å–∏–º—Ñ–æ–Ω–∏–∏.





–≠—Ç–æ—Ç –¥–æ–∂–¥—å —É–∂–µ –¥–∞–≤–Ω–æ –Ω–∞—á–∞–ª—Å—è, –¥–æ —Ç–æ–≥–æ –∫–∞–∫ —è —Ä–æ–¥–∏–ª—Å—è. –ü–æ –º–Ω–µ–Ω–∏—é —Å—Ç–∞—Ä–µ–π—à–∏–Ω, –¥–æ–∂–¥—å —à–µ–ª –µ—â–µ –¥–æ —Ç–æ–≥–æ, –∫–∞–∫ –æ–Ω–∏ –ø–æ—è–≤–∏–ª–∏—Å—å –Ω–∞ —Å–≤–µ—Ç





–î–æ–∂–¥—å –Ω–∏–∫–æ–≥–¥–∞ –Ω–µ –æ—Å—Ç–∞–Ω–∞–≤–ª–∏–≤–∞–ª—Å—è. –æ–Ω –ø–∞–¥–∞–µ—Ç –±–µ—Å–ø—Ä–∏—Å—Ç—Ä–∞—Å—Ç–Ω–æ, –∫–∞—Å–∞—è—Å—å –≤—Å–µ–≥–æ, —á—Ç–æ –Ω–∞—Ö–æ–¥–∏—Ç—Å—è –Ω–∞ –∑–µ–º–ª–µ, —É–Ω–æ—Å—è —Å —Å–æ–±–æ–π –≤—Å–µ—Ö –Ω–µ–æ—Å—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–∂–Ω—ã—Ö, –≤–µ–¥—è –∏—Ö –≤ —Ü–∞—Ä—Å—Ç–≤–æ –¥–æ–∂–¥—è. –ó—Ä–∏—Ç–µ–ª—è–º –∫–∞–∂–µ—Ç—Å—è, —á—Ç–æ —É–Ω–µ—Å–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–µ –¥–æ–∂–¥–µ–º –ª—é–¥–∏ —Å–ø—è—Ç, –∑–∞–ø–µ—Ä—Ç—ã –≤–æ —Å–Ω–∞—Ö, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–µ –Ω–∏–∫–æ–≥–¥–∞ –Ω–µ –∑–∞–∫–æ–Ω—á–∞—Ç—Å—è..





–õ—é–¥–∏ –∏—â—É—Ç —É–±–µ–∂–∏—â–∞, –≥–¥–µ —É–∫—Ä—ã–≤–∞—é—Ç—Å—è –≤ –ø–æ—Å—Ç—Ä–æ–π–∫–∞—Ö, –≤–æ–∑–≤–µ–¥–µ–Ω–Ω—ã—Ö –∏–∑ –ø—Ä–æ—á–Ω–æ–≥–æ –∂–µ–ª–µ–∑–æ–±–µ—Ç–æ–Ω–∞, –∏ –Ω–∞–¥–µ–≤–∞—é—Ç –æ–¥–µ–∂–¥—É, –∏–∑–≥–æ—Ç–æ–≤–ª–µ–Ω–Ω—É—é –∏–∑ —Ç–æ–ª—Å—Ç–æ–≥–æ, –≤–æ–¥–æ–Ω–µ–ø—Ä–æ–Ω–∏—Ü–∞–µ–º–æ–≥–æ –Ω–µ–π–ª–æ–Ω–æ–≤–æ–π —Ç–∫–∞–Ω–∏ -

–≤—Å–µ —ç—Ç–æ –≤ –ø–æ–ø—ã—Ç–∫–µ –Ω–µ –¥–∞—Ç—å —Å–µ–±–µ –∑–∞–±–ª—É–¥–∏—Ç—å—Å—è –≤ –±–µ—Å–∫–æ–Ω–µ—á–Ω—ã—Ö —Å–Ω–∞—Ö.





–Ø –Ω–∞–±–ª—é–¥–∞–ª –∑–∞ –Ω–∏–º–∏, –ª—é–¥–∏ –∂–∏–≤—É—â–∏–µ –≤ —Å—Ç—Ä–∞—Ö–µ –ø–æ–¥ –Ω–µ–ø—Ä–µ–∫—Ä–∞—â–∞—é—â–∏–º—Å—è –¥–æ–∂–¥–µ–º, –≤—ã–ø–æ–ª–Ω—è—é—â–∏–µ –æ–¥–Ω—É –∏ —Ç—É –∂–µ –∑–∞–¥–∞—á—É –∫–∞–∂–¥—ã–π –¥–µ–Ω—å: —Å–æ–±–∏—Ä–∞—é—Ç –µ–¥—É, —á–∏–Ω—è—Ç –æ–¥–µ–∂–¥—É, –∏ –ø–æ–¥–¥–µ—Ä–∂–∏–≤–∞—é—Ç —Å–≤–æ–∏ –¥–æ–º–∞‚Ä¶





—è –Ω–µ –∑–Ω–∞—é, —Å—á–∞—Å—Ç–ª–∏–≤–µ–µ –ª–∏ –º–∏—Ä –≤–Ω—É—Ç—Ä–∏ —Å–Ω–∞ –∏–ª–∏ —Ä–µ–∞–ª—å–Ω—ã–π –≤—Å–µ —Ç–∞–∫–∏ –ª—É—á—à–µ. –Ø –ø—Ä–æ—Å—Ç–æ –º–æ–ª—á–∞ —Å–ª—É—à–∞—é, –∫–∞–∫ –º–∏—Ä —Ä–∞–∑–≥–æ–≤–∞—Ä–∏–≤–∞–µ—Ç —Å –Ω–∞–º–∏ —Å –ø–æ–º–æ—â—å—é –¥–æ–∂–¥—è. —Ç—É–∫-—Ç—É–∫. –ì—Ä–æ—Ö–æ—Ç –∏ —Ä–µ–≤. –Ø —Å–ª—É—à–∞—é –≤ —Ç–∏—à–∏–Ω–µ.





–ö–∞–ø, –∫–∞–ø, –∫–∞–ø‚Ä¶





–î–æ–∂–¥—å –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç. –¢–µ—Ç—è –°—å—é–∑e–Ω –≤ —Å–æ—Å–µ–¥–Ω–µ–π –∫–∞–±–∏–Ω–∫–µ —Ä–æ–¥–∏–ª–∞ —Ä–µ–±–µ–Ω–∫–∞.





–í—Å–µ —Å–æ–±—Ä–∞–ª–∏—Å—å –≤–æ–∫—Ä—É–≥ –Ω–µ–µ c –≤–æ—Å—Ç–æ—Ä–≥–æ–º, —Å –≤–æ–æ–¥—É—à–µ–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏–µ–º –ø—Ä–∞–∑–¥–Ω—É—è —Ä–æ–∂–¥–µ–Ω–∏–µ —Ä–µ–±–µ–Ω–∫–∞.





–° —ç—Ç–æ–≥–æ –º–æ–º–µ–Ω—Ç–∞, –¢–µ—Ç—è –°—å—é–∑–µ–Ω –∫–∞–∂–µ—Ç—Å—è –ø—Ä–µ–≤—Ä–∞—â–∞–µ—Ç—Å—è –≤ –¥–µ–≤—É –ú–∞—Ä–∏—é.–ø–æ—Ç –∏ –∫—Ä–æ–≤—å –Ω–∞ –µ–µ —Ç–µ–ª–µ –ø—Ä–∏–æ–±—Ä–µ—Ç–∞—é—Ç –±–æ–∂–µ—Å—Ç–≤–µ–Ω–Ω–æ–µ —Å–≤–æ–π—Å—Ç–≤–æ, —Å—Ç–∞–Ω–æ–≤—è—Å—å —Å–∏–º–≤–æ–ª–∞–º–∏ –±–æ–ª–µ–∑–Ω–µ–Ω–Ω—ã—Ö —á—É–¥–µ—Å





–ë–∞–Ω–∫–µ—Ç –Ω–∞—á–∞–ª—Å—è. –í —ç—Ç–æ–º –∑–¥–∞–Ω–∏–∏, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–µ –º–æ–∂–µ—Ç –Ω–∞—Ö–æ–¥–∏—Ç—å—Å—è –Ω–∞ –≤—ã—Å–æ—Ç–µ –±–æ–ª–µ–µ —Å—Ç–∞ –º–µ—Ç—Ä–æ–≤, –ª—é–¥–∏ –ø—Ä–∏–Ω–æ—Å—è—Ç –ª—É—á—à–∏–µ –ø–æ–¥–∞—Ä–∫–∏ –∏ –µ–¥—É, –∫–∞–∫–∏–µ —Ç–æ–ª—å–∫–æ –º–æ–≥—É—Ç –Ω–∞–π—Ç–∏, –∏ —Å–∫–ª–∞–¥—ã–≤–∞—é—Ç –∏—Ö –Ω–∞ –º–µ—Ç–∞–ª–ª–∏—á–µ—Å–∫—É—é –∫—Ä–æ–≤–∞—Ç—å –°—å—é–∑–µ–Ω. –û–Ω–∞ —Å–ª–∞–±–æ —Å–º–æ—Ç—Ä–∏—Ç –Ω–∞ —à–æ–∫–æ–ª–∞–¥–Ω—ã–µ –∫–æ–Ω—Ñ–µ—Ç—ã, –≤—è–ª–µ–Ω–æ–µ –º—è—Å–æ –∏ –æ–¥–µ–∂–¥—É - –æ–¥–µ–∂–¥—É, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä–∞—è —Å–ª—É–∂–∏—Ç –Ω–µ –¥–ª—è –∑–∞—â–∏—Ç—ã, –∞ –¥–ª—è –≤–Ω–µ—à–Ω–µ–≥–æ –≤–∏–¥–∞. –í—Å–µ –æ–Ω–∏, –∫–∞–∫ –ø—Ä–∞–≤–∏–ª–æ, –≤—Å—Ç—Ä–µ—á–∞—é—Ç—Å—è —Ç–æ–ª—å–∫–æ –Ω–∞ –ø–æ–≤–µ—Ä—Ö–Ω–æ—Å—Ç–∏. –≠—Ç–∞ —É–ª—ã–±–∫–∞ —É–∫—Ä–∞—à–∞–µ—Ç –µ–µ –ª–∏—Ü–æ.





–ù–∞ —É–∂–∏–Ω–µ, –≥—Ä–∏–±—ã –∑–∞–º–µ—Ç–Ω–æ –æ—Ç—Å—É—Ç—Å—Ç–≤–æ–≤–∞–ª–∏. –≤–º–µ—Å—Ç–æ –Ω–∏—Ö –±—ã–ª —Å—ã—Ç–Ω—ã–π –º—è—Å–Ω–æ–π —Å—É–ø, –ø—Ä–∏–≥–æ—Ç–æ–≤–ª–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–π –∏–∑ –º–Ω–æ–∂–µ—Å—Ç–≤–∞ –Ω–µ–æ–ø–æ–∑–Ω–∞–Ω–Ω—ã—Ö –∫–æ—Ä–µ–Ω—å–µ–≤, –æ–≤–æ—â–µ–π –∏ —Å–ø–µ—Ü–∏–π. –ê—Ä–æ–º–∞—Ç —Å—É–ø–∞ –ø—Ä–æ–Ω–∏–∑—ã–≤–∞–µ—Ç –≤–µ—Å—å —ç—Ç–∞–∂, –ø–æ–≥—Ä—É–∂–∞—è –µ–≥–æ –≤ –≤–æ—Å—Ö–∏—Ç–∏—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω—ã–µ –∞—Ä–æ–º–∞—Ç—ã, –º–æ–º–µ–Ω—Ç–∞–ª—å–Ω–æ —É—Å—Ç—Ä–∞–Ω—è—è —Å—ã—Ä–æ—Å—Ç—å –∏ –∑–∞—Ç—Ö–ª–æ—Å—Ç—å, —Ü–∞—Ä—è—â—É—é –≤ –ø–æ–º–µ—â–µ–Ω–∏—è—Ö





–ª–æ–∂–∫–∞ –∑–∞ –ª–æ–∂–∫–æ–π, –≥–æ—Ä—è—á–∏–π —Å—É–ø —Å–æ–≥—Ä–µ–≤–∞–ª –∏—Ö –∂–∏–≤–æ—Ç—ã –∏ –æ–±–ª–µ–≥—á–∞–ª –¥—É—à–µ–≤–Ω—ã–µ —Å—Ç—Ä–∞–¥–∞–Ω–∏—è. –í—Å–∫–æ—Ä–µ, –∫–∞—Å—Ç—Ä—é–ª—è –æ–ø—É—Å—Ç–µ–ª–∞. –õ—é–¥–∏ —Å–æ–±—Ä–∞–ª–∏—Å—å –≤–æ–∫—Ä—É–≥ –∫–æ—Å—Ç—Ä–∞, –ø–æ–ø–∏–≤–∞—è –æ—Å–æ–±—ã–π —Å–ø–∏—Ä—Ç–Ω–æ–π –Ω–∞–ø–∏—Ç–æ–∫, –Ω–∞—Å—Ç–æ—è–Ω–Ω—ã–π –Ω–∞ –≥—Ä–∏–±–∞—Ö - –ø—Ä–∏ —ç—Ç–æ–º –Ω–µ–ø—Ä–∏–Ω—É–∂–¥–µ–Ω–Ω–æ –±–æ–ª—Ç–∞—è –æ —Ç–æ–º, —á—Ç–æ –±—ã–≤–∞–µ—Ç —Ç–æ–ª—å–∫–æ –≤–æ —Å–Ω–µ





–æ–≥–æ–Ω—å –≤ –∫–æ–Ω—Ü–µ –∫–æ–Ω—Ü–æ–≤ –ø–æ—Ç—É—Ö –∏ –ª—é–¥–∏ –Ω–∞—á–∞–ª–∏ —Ä–∞–∑—Ö–æ–¥–∏—Ç—å—Å—è .





–ù–æ –°—å—é–∑–µ–Ω –µ—â–µ –Ω–µ –ø–æ–ø—Ä–æ–±–æ–≤–∞–ª–∞ –µ–µ —Å—É–ø. –†–∞–¥–æ—Å—Ç—å, –≤—ã–∑–≤–∞–Ω–Ω–∞—è –ë–∞–Ω–∫–µ—Ç–æ–º, –ø–æ—Å—Ç–µ–ø–µ–Ω–Ω–æ —Ä–∞—Å—Å–µ—è–ª–∞—Å—å.





–õ—é–¥–∏ –≤–µ—Ä–Ω—É–ª–∏—Å—å –∫ —Å–≤–æ–∏–º –ø–æ–≤—Å–µ–¥–Ω–µ–≤–Ω—ã–º –¥–µ–ª–∞–º: —Å–æ–±–∏—Ä–∞—Ç—å –µ–¥—É, —á–∏–Ω–∏—Ç—å –æ–¥–µ–∂–¥—É, –∏ –ø–æ–¥–¥–µ—Ä–∂–∏–≤–∞—Ç—å —Å–≤–æ–∏ –¥–æ–º–∞ –≤ –±–µ–∑–æ–ø–∞—Å–Ω–æ—Å—Ç–∏‚Ä¶





–ï—Å–ª–∏ —á—Ç–æ-—Ç–æ –∏–∑–º–µ–Ω–∏–ª–æ—Å—å, –≤–æ–∑–º–æ–∂–Ω–æ –∏–∑-–∑–∞ —Ç–æ–≥–æ, —á—Ç–æ –≤–æ –≤—Ä–µ–º—è –æ–±–µ–¥–∞ –ª—é–¥–∏ –º–æ–≥–ª–∏ –Ω–∞—Å–ª–∞–∂–¥–∞—Ç—å—Å—è –Ω–µ—Å–∫–æ–ª—å–∫–∏–º–∏ –∫—É—Å–æ—á–∫–∞–º–∏ –æ—Å—Ç–∞–≤—à–µ–≥–æ—Å—è –≤—è–ª–µ–Ω–æ–≥–æ –º—è—Å–∞ –∏ –≥—Ä–∏–±–Ω–æ–π –Ω–∞—Å—Ç–æ–π–∫–æ–π —Å –±–∞–Ω–∫–µ—Ç–∞.





–°—å—é–∑–µ–Ω –ø—Ä–æ–¥–æ–ª–∂–∞–ª–∞ –≤–æ—Å—Å—Ç–∞–Ω–∞–≤–ª–∏–≤–∞—Ç—å—Å—è –Ω–∞ –∫—Ä–æ–≤–∞—Ç–∏, —Å –æ—Ç—è–≥–æ—â–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–º –≤–∏–¥–æ–º, –ø–æ—Å–ª–µ —Ä–æ–¥–æ–≤. –ï–µ —Ä–µ–±–µ–Ω–∫–∞ –ø–µ—Ä–µ–Ω–µ—Å–ª–∏ –≤ –¥—Ä—É–≥—É—é –∫–æ–º–Ω–∞—Ç—É, –Ω–∞–¥–µ–∂–Ω–æ —É–∫—Ä—ã—Ç—ã–π –≤ –¥–µ—Ä–µ–≤—è–Ω–Ω–æ–π –∫—Ä–æ–≤–∞—Ç–∫–µ. –ü–æ—Å–∫–æ–ª—å–∫—É –°—å—é–∑–∞–Ω –±—ã–ª–∞ —Å–ª–∏—à–∫–æ–º —Å–ª–∞–±–∞, –ª—é–¥—è–º —É–¥–∞–ª–æ—Å—å –Ω–∞—Å–∫—Ä–µ—Å—Ç–∏ –Ω–µ–º–Ω–æ–≥–æ –ø–æ—Ä–æ—à–∫–æ–æ–±—Ä–∞–∑–Ω–æ–π —Å–º–µ—Å–∏ –¥–ª—è —Ä–µ–±–µ–Ω–∫–∞.





–†–µ–±–µ–Ω–∫–∞ –µ—â–µ —Ç–∞–∫ –∏ –Ω–µ –Ω–∞–∑–≤–∞–ª–∏. –û–Ω —Å–æ—Å–µ—Ç –±—É—Ç—ã–ª–æ—á–∫—É, –µ–≥–æ –≥–ª–∞–∑–∞ –±—ã–ª–∏ –Ω–∞–ø–æ–ª–Ω–µ–Ω—ã –Ω–µ–≤–∏–Ω–Ω–æ—Å—Ç—å—é.





–ú—É–∂ –°—å—é–∑–µ–Ω–∞, –∏—Å–ø—ã—Ç–∞–≤ –ø–µ—Ä–≤–æ–Ω–∞—á–∞–ª—å–Ω—É—é —Ä–∞–¥–æ—Å—Ç—å –æ—Ç —Ç–æ–≥–æ, —á—Ç–æ —Å—Ç–∞–ª –æ—Ç—Ü–æ–º, –æ–Ω —Ç–µ–ø–µ—Ä—å –æ–±—Ä–µ–º–µ–Ω–µ–Ω –∑–∞–±–æ—Ç–∞–º–∏. –ü–æ–ø–æ–ª–Ω–µ–Ω–∏–µ –≤ —Å–µ–º—å–µ - —ç—Ç–æ –µ—â–µ –æ–¥–∏–Ω —Ä–æ—Ç, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–π –Ω—É–∂–Ω–æ –∫–æ—Ä–º–∏—Ç—å. –ú–∞—Ç—å –ø–æ–∫–∞ —á—Ç–æ –º–æ–∂–µ—Ç –∫–æ—Ä–º–∏—Ç—å —Ä–µ–±–µ–Ω–∫–∞ –≥—Ä—É–¥—å—é, –Ω–æ –∫–∞–∫ –ø–æ—Ç–æ–º –æ–Ω–∏ —Å–º–æ–≥—É—Ç –Ω–∞–π—Ç–∏ –µ–¥—É?





–û–Ω —Ä–∞—Å—Ö–∞–∂–∏–≤–∞–µ—Ç –≤–∑–∞–¥-–≤–ø–µ—Ä–µ–¥ –ø–æ –∏—Ö —Ç–µ—Å–Ω–æ–π –∫–∞–±–∏–Ω–∫–µ, –≤–¥—Ä—É–≥ –≤—Å–ø–æ–º–Ω–∏–≤, —á—Ç–æ –ª—é–¥–∏ –Ω–∞ –ø–æ–≤–µ—Ä—Ö–Ω–æ—Å—Ç–∏ —Å—Ç—Ä–æ—è—Ç –∫–∞–∫—É—é-—Ç–æ –º–∞—à–∏–Ω—É –∏ –∏–º –Ω—É–∂–Ω—ã –¥–æ–ø–æ–ª–Ω–∏—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω—ã–µ —Ä–∞–±–æ—á–∏–µ —Ä—É–∫–∏. –ü–æ —Å–ª—É—Ö–∞–º, —Ä–µ–≥–∏—Å—Ç—Ä–∞—Ü–∏—è –ø–æ–∑–≤–æ–ª—è–µ—Ç –≤–∑—è—Ç—å —Å —Å–æ–±–æ–π –∫–æ–º–ø–∞–Ω—å–æ–Ω–∞ –∏ –ø–µ—Ä–µ—Å–µ–ª–∏—Ç—å—Å—è –Ω–∞ –ø–æ–≤–µ—Ä—Ö–Ω–æ—Å—Ç—å –¥–ª—è –ø—Ä–æ–∂–∏–≤–∞–Ω–∏—è.

–¢–∞–∫ —á—Ç–æ —ç—Ç–æ –º–æ–π —Å–æ–Ω. –£–¥–∏–≤–∏—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω–æ–µ —Å—Ö–æ–¥—Å—Ç–≤–æ

‚Äú–ß—É–≤—Å—Ç–≤—É–µ—à—å —Å–µ–±—è –æ–¥–∏–Ω–æ–∫–æ?‚Äù –í–æ–∑–Ω–∏–∫ –Ω–µ–∂–Ω—ã–π –∏ —É—Å–ø–æ–∫–∞–∏–≤–∞—é—â–∏–π –≥–æ–ª–æ—Å





‚Äú–ö—Ç–æ —Ç—ã?‚Äù —Å–ø—Ä–æ—Å–∏–ª —è





‚Äú–Ø - —ç—Ç–æ —Ç—ã, —Ç–æ—Ç, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–≥–æ —Ç—ã –Ω–µ –≤–∏–¥–∏—à—å‚Äù





–Ø –æ—Å–æ–∑–Ω–∞–ª, —á—Ç–æ —ç—Ç–æ –º–æ–π –≥–æ–ª–æ—Å





‚Äú–¢—ã —ç—Ç–æ‚Ä¶—è?‚Äù





‚Äú–¥–∞, –º—ã –∫–∞–∫ –¥–≤–µ —Å—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–Ω—ã –æ–¥–Ω–æ–π –º–æ–Ω–µ—Ç—ã. –Ø —Å—É—â–µ—Å—Ç–≤—É—é –±–ª–∞–≥–æ–¥–∞—Ä—è —Ç–µ–±–µ, –ø–æ—è–≤–ª—è—é—Å—å —Ç–∞–∫, –∫–∞–∫ —Ç—ã –¥—É–º–∞–µ—à—å. –Ø –∑–Ω–∞—é, —á—Ç–æ —Ç—ã –∑–Ω–∞–µ—à—å. –ò –∑–Ω–∞—é, —á—Ç–æ —Ç—ã —Ö–æ—á–µ—à—å‚Äù





‚Äú–Ø —Ö–æ—á—É‚Ä¶—á—Ç–æ –∏–º–µ–Ω–Ω–æ —è —Ö–æ—á—É?‚Äù





‚Äú–ù–∞–ø—Ä–∞–≤–ª—è–πc—è –∫ —Å–≤–µ—Ç—É. –¢–∞–º —Ç—ã –Ω–∞–π–¥–µ—à—å –æ—Ç–≤–µ—Ç—ã –Ω–∞ —Å–≤–æ–∏ –≤–æ–ø—Ä–æ—Å—ã‚Äù





–ó–∞—Ç–µ–º –≥–æ–ª–æ—Å –∑–∞—Ç–∏—Ö.





–í–¥–∞–ª–∏ –±–ª–µ—Å—Ç–∏—Ç –æ–ª–æ–≤–æ, –∏ —è –∏–¥—É –∫ –Ω–µ–º—É.





‚Ä¶





–Ø —Å—Ç—É–ø–∞—é –ø–æ –±–µ—Å–ø–ª–æ—Ç–Ω–æ–π, –≤–∞—Ç–Ω–æ–π –∑–µ–º–ª–µ, –Ω–µ –∏–∑–¥–∞–≤–∞—è –Ω–∏ –∑–≤—É–∫–∞, –Ω–µ –∑–Ω–∞—è –∫–∞–∫ –¥–∞–ª–µ–∫–∞ —è –ø—Ä–æ–π–¥—É. –ù–æ–≥–∏ –±–æ–ª—è—Ç, –º–æ–∏ –∫–æ–ª–µ–Ω–∏ —Å–≤–æ–¥–∏—Ç —Å—É–¥–æ—Ä–æ–≥–æ–π, –∞ –¥—ã—Ö–∞–Ω–∏–µ —Å—Ç–∞–Ω–æ–≤–∏—Ç—Å—è —Ç—è–∂–µ–ª—ã–º. –°–≤–µ—Ç –≤–ø–µ—Ä–µ–¥–∏ –Ω–µ –∫–∞–∂–µ—Ç—Å—è –±–ª–∏–∂–µ.





–Ø –ø—Ä–æ–¥–æ–ª–∂–∞—é –∏–¥—Ç–∏, –≤ –≥–æ—Ä–ª–µ –ø–æ—è–≤–ª—è–µ—Ç—Å—è –º–µ—Ç–∞–ª–ª–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–∏–π –ø—Ä–∏–≤–∫—É—Å, –∑—Ä–µ–Ω–∏–µ –∑–∞—Ç—É–º–∞–Ω–∏–≤–∞–µ—Ç—Å—è, –∏ –¥–∞–∂–µ –Ω–µ –ø–æ–ª—É—á–∞–µ—Ç—Å—è –ø–æ–¥–Ω—è—Ç—å –≥–æ–ª–æ–≤—É. –Ø –≤—Å–µ –µ—â–µ –ø—Ä–æ–¥–æ–ª–∂–∞—é –ø–æ–¥–Ω–∏–º–∞—Ç—å—Å—è.

‚Äú–ü—Ä–∏–∫–æ—Å–Ω–∏—Å—å –∫ –Ω–µ–º—É‚Äù –í–æ –º–Ω–µ –∑–∞—Ä–æ–∂–¥–∞–µ—Ç—Å—è –º—ã—Å–ª—å, –∏ —è –ø–æ–¥—á–∏–Ω—è—é—Å—å –µ–π.





–û–≥–Ω–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–π —à–∞—Ä –Ω–µ –æ–±–∂–∏–≥–∞–µ—Ç –º–µ–Ω—è, –∞, –Ω–∞–æ–±–æ—Ä–æ—Ç, –Ω–µ–∂–Ω–æ –æ–±–Ω–∏–º–∞–µ—Ç –º–æ—é —Ä—É–∫—É.





–¢–µ–ø–ª–æ –ø—Ä–∏–ª–∏–≤–∞–µ—Ç –∫–æ –º–Ω–µ, —Å–æ–ø—Ä–æ–≤–æ–∂–¥–∞–µ–º–æ–µ —ç–º–æ—Ü–∏—è–º–∏





–Ø –∏—â—É –∏—Ö, –±–µ–∑—Ä–∞—Å—Å—É–¥–Ω–æ –±—Ä–æ—Å–∞—è—Å—å –≤ —à–∞—Ä, –ø–æ–∫–∞ –≤—Å–µ –º–æ–µ —Ç–µ–ª–æ –Ω–µ –ø–æ–≥—Ä—É–∑–∏—Ç—Å—è –≤ –Ω–µ–≥–æ.





–°–∏—è–Ω–∏–µ –æ–∫—Ä—É–∂–∞–µ—Ç –º–µ–Ω—è, —Ç–µ–ø–ª—ã–µ –ø–æ—Ç–æ–∫–∏ –æ–±–Ω–∏–º–∞—é—Ç –º–µ–Ω—è, –∞ —ç–º–æ—Ü–∏–∏ –±—É—Ä–ª—è—Ç –≤–Ω—É—Ç—Ä–∏, –æ–∫—Ä–∞—à–∏–≤–∞—è —Ç—å–º—É –≤ –º–∏—Ä–∏–∞–¥—ã –æ—Ç—Ç–µ–Ω–∫–æ–≤.





–í–µ—Å–µ–ª—å–µ, –±–æ–ª—å, –ø–µ—á–∞–ª—å, —É–¥–æ–≤–ª–µ—Ç–≤–æ—Ä–µ–Ω–∏–µ, —Ä–∞–∑–æ—á–∞—Ä–æ–≤–∞–Ω–∏–µ, –≤–æ—Å—Ö–∏—â–µ–Ω–∏–µ, –∑–∞–≤–∏—Å—Ç—å.





–í –æ—Å–ª–µ–ø–∏—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω–æ–º —Å–≤–µ—Ç–µ, –º–æ–µ —Å–æ–∑–Ω–∞–Ω–∏–µ —Å–Ω–æ–≤–∞ –ø—Ä–µ—Ä—ã–≤–∞–µ—Ç—Å—è.





‚Ä¶





–ó–≤—É–∫ –ø—Ä–æ–ª–∏–≤–Ω–æ–≥–æ –¥–æ–∂–¥—è.





–ö–∞–ø–ª–∏ –ø–∞–¥–∞—é—Ç –Ω–∞ –º–æ—é —â–µ–∫–∏, —Å–æ–∑–¥–∞–≤–∞—è –∑–≤—É–∫, –ø–æ—Ö–æ–∂–∏–π –Ω–∞ —Ç–æ–ø–æ—Ç.





–Ø –æ—Ç–∫—Ä—ã–ª –≥–ª–∞–∑–∞ - —è –Ω–∞ –∫—Ä—ã—à–µ. –ù–∞–≤–µ—Ä–Ω–æ–µ, —è –≤–µ—Ä–Ω—É–ª—Å—è –∏–∑ —Å–Ω–∞.

‚Äú–ö—Ç–æ —Ç—ã? –∏ –≥–¥–µ —è?‚Äù





–°–ø—Ä–æ—Å–∏–ª –º–µ–Ω—è —Å–∑–∞–¥–∏ –¥–µ–≤—á–∞—á–∏–π –≥–æ–ª–æ—Å.





–Ø –ø–æ–≤–µ—Ä–Ω—É–ª—Å—è. –Æ–Ω–∞—è –¥–µ–≤–æ—á–∫–∞ –≤ –±–µ–ª–æ–º –ø–ª–∞—Ç—å–µ —Å—Ç–æ—è–ª–∞ –ø–µ—Ä–µ–¥–æ –º–Ω–æ–π. –ö–∞–ø–ª–∏ –ø–∞–¥–∞–ª–∏ –Ω–∞ –Ω–µ–µ, –Ω–æ –æ–Ω–∏ –Ω–µ –æ–º—Ä–∞—á–∞—é—Ç –µ–µ –ø–ª–∞—Ç—å–µ –∏ –±–µ–ª—ã—Ö –Ω–∏—Å–ø–∞–¥–∞—é—â–∏—Ö –≤–æ–ª–æ—Å.





–ï–µ –≥–æ–ª—É–±—ã–µ –≥–ª–∞–∑–∞ —Å –±–ª–µ–¥–Ω—ã–º–∏ –≤–æ–ª–æ—Å–∞–º–∏ —É—Å—Ç—Ä–µ–º–ª–µ–Ω—ã –Ω–∞ –º–µ–Ω—è.





‚Äú–ü–æ—á–µ–º—É —Ç—ã –ø–ª–∞—á–µ—à—å?‚Äù





–û–Ω–∞ –æ—Ç–≤–µ—Ç–∏–ª–∞.



–ì–ª–∞–≤–∞ 1: –î–≤–µ —Å—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–Ω—ã: –≥–æ—Ä—å–∫–∞—è –∏ —Å–ª–∞–¥–∫–∞—è ‚Äã

  • ‚Ä¶
  • (–ù–µ—Å–º–æ—Ç—Ä—è –Ω–∞ —Ç–æ, —á—Ç–æ —É –º–µ–Ω—è –±—ã–ª–æ –º–Ω–æ–≥–æ –≤–æ–ø—Ä–æ—Å–æ–≤, –Ω–∞–º –Ω—É–∂–Ω–æ –≤–æ–π—Ç–∏ –≤–Ω—É—Ç—Ä—å. –≠—Ç—É —Å—Ü–µ–Ω—É –Ω–µ –¥–æ–ª–∂–µ–Ω —É–≤–∏–¥–µ—Ç—å –Ω–∏–∫—Ç–æ –¥—Ä—É–≥–æ–π.)
  • (–Ø –±—ã—Å—Ç—Ä–æ –æ–±—ä—è—Å–Ω—è—é –ø–æ—á–µ–º—É –≤—Å–µ –¥–æ–ª–∂–Ω—ã –∏–∑–±–µ–≥–∞—Ç—å –¥–æ–∂–¥—è. –ü–æ–∫–∞ —è –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏–ª –æ–± —ç—Ç–æ–º, —è –∑–∞–º–µ—Ç–∏–ª, —á—Ç–æ –µ–µ –æ–¥–µ–∂–¥–∞ –Ω–µ –±—ã–ª–∞ –º–æ–∫—Ä–æ–π.)
  • (–ú–æ—è –æ–¥–µ–∂–¥–∞ —É–∂–µ –ø–æ—á—Ç–∏ –≤—ã—Å–æ—Ö–ª–∞ –æ—Ç —Ç–µ–ø–ª–∞ –º–æ–µ–≥–æ —Ç–µ–ª–∞. –î–∞–∂–µ –µ—Å–ª–∏ —è —Ö–æ—á—É –ø—Ä–∏—Å–æ–µ–¥–∏–Ω–∏—Ç—å—Å—è –∫ –æ—Å—Ç–∞–ª—å–Ω—ã–º, —è –Ω–µ –º–æ–≥—É –ø—Ä–æ—Å—Ç–æ –æ—Å—Ç–∞–≤–∏—Ç—å —ç—Ç—É –¥–µ–≤—É—à–∫—É –æ–¥–Ω—É).

1-2 ‚Äã

  • –ù—É, –Ø –ø—Ä–∏–Ω–µ—Å —Å–≤–µ–∂–µ–≤—ã–ø–µ—á–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–µ –≥—Ä–∏–±—ã. –û–Ω–∏ –ø–æ—Å—ã–ø–∞–Ω—ã –ø–µ—Ä—Ü–µ–º –∏ –≤–∫—É—Å –¥–æ–ª–∂–µ–Ω –±—ã—Ç—å –Ω–æ—Ä–º–∞–ª—å–Ω—ã–º. –ò –≤–æ—Ç —Å–±–æ—Ä–Ω–∏–∫ —Å —Ä–∞–∑–Ω—ã–º–∏ –∏—Å—Ç–æ—Ä–∏—è–º–∏.
  • –¢—ã —Ç—É—Ç.
  • (–Ø —Å—Ç–æ—é —É –¥–≤–µ—Ä–∏ –º–∞–ª–µ–Ω—å–∫–æ–π –∫–æ–º–Ω–∞—Ç—ã –∏ —Å—Ç—É—á—É –≤ –æ–ø—Ä–µ–¥–µ–ª–µ–Ω–Ω–æ–º —Ä–∏—Ç–º–µ. –≠—Ç–æ –Ω–∞—à —Å–æ–≥–ª–∞—Å–æ–≤–∞–Ω–Ω—ã–π —Å–∏–≥–Ω–∞–ª - –µ—Å–ª–∏ —Å—Ç—É–∫ –Ω–µ —Ç–∞–∫–æ–π, —Ç–æ –æ–Ω–∞ –¥–æ–ª–∂–Ω–∞ —Å–ø—Ä—è—Ç–∞—Ç—å—Å—è).
  • (–° —Ç–µ—Ö –ø–æ—Ä –≤—Ä–µ–º—è –ø—Ä–æ–ª–µ—Ç–µ–ª–æ –±—ã—Å—Ç—Ä–æ. –ö–∞–∂–¥—ã–π –¥–µ–Ω—å —è –ø—Ä–∏–Ω–æ—à—É –µ–π –µ–¥—É –∏ –∫–Ω–∏–≥–∏, –∏, –∫–∞–∂–µ—Ç—Å—è, –¥–µ–≤—É—à–∫–∞ –ø–æ—Å—Ç–µ–ø–µ–Ω–Ω–æ –ø—Ä–∏–≤—ã–∫–∞–µ—Ç –∫ —ç—Ç–æ–π –∂–∏–∑–Ω–∏).
  • –ì—Ä–∏–±—ã. –°–Ω–æ–≤–∞.
  • –Ø –∑–Ω–∞—é, –Ω–æ –±–æ–ª—å—à–µ –∑–¥–µ—Å—å –µ—Å—Ç—å –Ω–µ—á–µ–≥–æ. –•–æ—Ä–æ—à–∞—è –µ–¥–∞ –ø–æ—è–≤–ª—è–µ—Ç—Å—è —Ç–æ–ª—å–∫–æ –≤–æ –≤—Ä–µ–º—è —Ñ–µ—Å—Ç–∏–≤–∞–ª–µ–π –∏ –ø—Ä–∞–∑–¥–Ω–∏–∫–æ–≤. –õ–∏–±–æ –µ—à—å, –ª–∏–±–æ –≥–æ–ª–æ–¥–∞–π.
  • '—Ñ–µ—Å—Ç–∏–≤–∞–ª—å'?
  • –≠—Ç–æ..–∫–æ–≥–¥–∞ –ø—Ä–æ–∏–∑–æ—à–ª–æ —á—Ç–æ-—Ç–æ —Ö–æ—Ä–æ—à–µ–µ –∏ –≤—Å–µ —Å–æ–±–∏—Ä–∞—é—Ç—Å—è, —á—Ç–æ–±—ã –ø–æ–µ—Å—Ç—å –≤–∫—É—Å–Ω–æ–π –µ–¥—ã.
  • –ï—Å–ª–∏ –±—ã–ª–∞ –±—ã –≤–æ–∑–º–æ–∂–Ω–æ—Å—Ç—å, —è –±—ã –º–æ–≥ –ø—Ä–∏–Ω–µ—Å—Ç–∏ –≤–∞–º —á—Ç–æ-–Ω–∏–±—É–¥—å –¥—Ä—É–≥–æ–µ‚Ä¶
  • –ó–∞–ø–µ—á–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–µ –≥—Ä–∏–±—ã —Ç–æ–∂–µ –ø–æ–¥–æ–π–¥—É—Ç.
  • –ü—Ä–∞–≤–¥–∞? –õ—é–¥–∏ –∑–¥–µ—Å—å —É–∂–µ —É—Å—Ç–∞–ª–∏ –æ—Ç –Ω–∏—Ö
  • (–Ø –∫–ª–∞–¥—É –∑–∞–≤–µ—Ä–Ω—É—Ç—ã–µ –≥—Ä–∏–±—ã –Ω–∞ —Å—Ç–æ–ª –∏ –∑–∞–º–µ—á–∞—é, —á—Ç–æ –∫–Ω–∏–≥–∏, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–µ —è –ø—Ä–∏–Ω–µ—Å –µ–π —Ä–∞–Ω—å—à–µ, –æ—Å—Ç–∞–ª–∏—Å—å –Ω–µ—Ç—Ä–æ–Ω—É—Ç—ã–º–∏).
  • –¢—ã‚Ä¶–Ω–µ –º–æ–∂–µ—à—å –ø–æ–Ω—è—Ç—å —Å–æ–¥–µ—Ä–∂–∞–Ω–∏–µ?
  • –ù–µ—Ç.
  • –ü–æ–Ω—è–ª‚Ä¶–≤–æ—Ç, –≤–æ–∑—å–º–∏.
  • (–û–Ω–∞ –±–µ—Ä–µ—Ç —Ñ–æ—Ç–æ–≥—Ä–∞—Ñ–∏—é, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—É—é —è –µ–π –ø—Ä–æ—Ç—è–≥–∏–≤–∞—é. –û–Ω–∞ –ø–æ–∂–µ–ª—Ç–µ–ª–∞ –∏ –≤—ã—Ü–≤–µ–ª–∞, –Ω–æ –ø–µ–π–∑–∞–∂ –ø–æ-–ø—Ä–µ–∂–Ω–µ–º—É –ø—Ä–µ–∫—Ä–∞—Å–µ–Ω).
  • ‚Ä¶
  • (–ï–µ –≥–ª–∞–∑–∞ —Å–ª–µ–≥–∫–∞ —Ä–∞—Å—à–∏—Ä–∏–ª–∏—Å—å, —Å–ª–æ–≤–Ω–æ –±—ã–ª–∏ –ø—Ä–∏–≤–ª–µ—á–µ–Ω—ã.)
  • –û—á–µ–Ω—å –∫—Ä–∞—Å–∏–≤–æ. –ß—Ç–æ —ç—Ç–æ?
  • –≠—Ç–∏ —Ñ–æ—Ç–æ–≥—Ä–∞—Ñ–∏–∏ —Å –º–µ—Å—Ç–∞–º–∏ –∏–∑ —Ä–∞–∑–Ω—ã—Ö —É–≥–æ–ª–∫–æ–≤ –º–∏—Ä–∞. –ù–æ –∏—Ö‚Ä¶–±–æ–ª—å—à–µ –Ω–µ—Ç. –û—Å—Ç–∞–ª–∏—Å—å —Ç–æ–ª—å–∫–æ —Ñ–æ—Ç–æ–≥—Ä–∞—Ñ–∏–∏ —Å –Ω–∏–º–∏.
  • –ï—Å–ª–∏ –Ω—Ä–∞–≤–∏—Ç—Å—è, —Ç–æ —è –º–æ–≥—É –ø—Ä–∏–Ω–µ—Å—Ç–∏ –±–æ–ª—å—à–µ —Ñ–æ—Ç–æ–≥—Ä–∞—Ñ–∏–π –∏–∑ –¥—Ä—É–≥–∏—Ö –º–µ—Å—Ç
  • –ö–æ–Ω–µ—á–Ω–æ‚Ä¶!
  • (–° —Ç–µ—Ö –ø–æ—Ä, –Ø —á–∞—â–µ —Å—Ç–∞–ª –ø—Ä–∏–Ω–æ—Å–∏—Ç—å —Ñ–æ—Ç–æ–≥—Ä–∞—Ñ–∏–∏ –∏ –∞–ª—å–±–æ–º—ã. –ï–π –æ—á–µ–Ω—å –Ω—Ä–∞–≤–∏–ª–æ—Å—å —Å–º–æ—Ç—Ä–µ—Ç—å –Ω–∞ –Ω–∏—Ö. –í –∫–æ–Ω—Ü–µ –∫–æ–Ω—Ü–æ–≤, –∫–æ–≥–æ –Ω–µ –æ—á–∞—Ä–æ–≤—ã–≤–∞–µ—Ç –ø—Ä–µ–∫—Ä–∞—Å–Ω–æ–µ, —É—Ç—Ä–∞—á–µ–Ω–Ω–æ–µ –ø—Ä–æ—à–ª–æ–µ?)
  • (–°–µ–≥–æ–¥–Ω—è, —è –ø–ª–∞–Ω–∏—Ä—É—é –ø—Ä–∏–Ω–µ—Å—Ç–∏ –µ—â–µ —Ñ–æ—Ç–æ–≥—Ä–∞—Ñ–∏–π –∏ –µ–¥—É, –∫–∞–∫ –æ–±—ã—á–Ω–æ.)
  • (–î–æ–π–¥—è –¥–æ –ª–µ—Å—Ç–Ω–∏—Ü—ã, —è –≤–∏–∂—É, —á—Ç–æ –æ–Ω–∞ —Å—Ç–æ–∏—Ç —Ç–∞–º —Å –ø–æ—Ç–µ—Ä—è–Ω–Ω—ã–º –≤–∏–¥–æ–º.)
  • –ü—Ä–∏–≤–µ—Ç, —á—Ç–æ‚Ä¶ —á—Ç–æ —Ç—ã —Ç—É—Ç –¥–µ–ª–∞–µ—à—å!?
  • –Ø —É—Ö–æ–∂—É. –Ø —Ö–æ—á—É —É–π—Ç–∏ –æ—Ç—Å—é–¥–∞, —É–≤–∏–¥–µ—Ç—å –º–∏—Ä –∫–∞–∫ –Ω–∞ —ç—Ç–∏—Ö —Ñ–æ—Ç–æ–≥—Ä–∞—Ñ–∏—è—Ö. –Ø –Ω–µ —Ö–æ—á—É –±–æ–ª—å—à–µ –æ—Å—Ç–∞–≤–∞—Ç—å—Å—è –≤ —ç—Ç–æ–π –∂—É—Ç–∫–æ–π –∫–æ–º–Ω–∞—Ç—É—à–∫–µ.
  • ‚Ä¶‚Ä¶
  • (–í–µ—Ä–Ω–æ. –ù–∏–∫—Ç–æ –Ω–µ –∑–∞—Ö–æ—á–µ—Ç –≤–µ—á–Ω–æ —Å–∏–¥–µ—Ç—å –≤ –∫—Ä–æ—à–µ—á–Ω–æ–º –ø—Ä–æ—Å—Ç—Ä–∞–Ω—Å—Ç–≤–µ. –û–Ω–∞ —Ö–æ—á–µ—Ç –≤—ã–±—Ä–∞—Ç—å—Å—è. –ò –≤—Å—ë –±—É–¥–µ—Ç —Ö–æ—Ä–æ—à–æ, –µ—Å–ª–∏ –Ω–∏–∫—Ç–æ –Ω–µ –Ω–∞–π–¥–µ—Ç –µ—ë –∑–¥–µ—Å—å‚Ä¶
  • –ü–æ–¥–æ–∂–¥–∏ –º–µ–Ω—è –∑–¥–µ—Å—å. –Ø –≤–æ–∑—å–º—É —Å–≤–æ—é –ø–∞–ª—å—Ç–æ, —á—Ç–æ–±—ã –ø—Ä–∏–∫—Ä—ã—Ç—å—Å—è. –¢–µ–±—è –ø–æ–π–º–∞—é—Ç, –µ—Å–ª–∏ —Ç—ã –±—É–¥–µ—à—å —Ö–æ–¥–∏—Ç—å –≤ —Ç–∞–∫–æ–º –≤–∏–¥–µ.
  • –¢—ã –º–µ–Ω—è –æ—Ç–≤–µ–¥—ë—à—å –Ω–∞—Ä—É–∂—É?
  • –Ø –æ–±–µ—â–∞—é.
  • –°–ø–∞—Å–∏–±–æ.
  • (–ú–Ω–µ –ø—Ä–∏—Ö–æ–¥–∏—Ç—Å—è "–æ–¥–æ–ª–∂–∏—Ç—å" –ø–ª–∞—â —É —Å–ª–µ—Å–∞—Ä—è, –µ–≥–æ –ø–ª–æ—Ç–Ω–æ–π —Ç–µ–º–Ω–æ–π —Ç–∫–∞–Ω–∏ –¥–æ—Å—Ç–∞—Ç–æ—á–Ω–æ, —á—Ç–æ–±—ã —Å–∫—Ä—ã—Ç—å –ª–∏—Ü–æ –∏ —Ç–µ–ª–æ).
  • –ü–æ–º–Ω–∏, –Ω–µ —Å–Ω–∏–º–∞–π –∫–∞–ø—é—à–æ–Ω, –æ–±–µ—â–∞–π –º–Ω–µ.
  • –•–æ—Ä–æ—à–æ.
  • (–ú—ã –ø–æ–∫–∏–¥–∞–µ–º –ª–µ—Å—Ç–Ω–∏—á–Ω—É—é –∫–ª–µ—Ç–∫—É, –ø—Ä–æ—Ö–æ–¥—è —á–µ—Ä–µ–∑ –∏–º–ø—Ä–æ–≤–∏–∑–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞–Ω–Ω—ã–µ –±–∞—Ä—å–µ—Ä—ã –∏–∑ –º–µ—à–∫–æ–≤ —Å –ø–µ—Å–∫–æ–º –∏ –≤—ã–±—Ä–æ—à–µ–Ω–Ω–æ–π –º–µ–±–µ–ª–∏, –∏ –ø–æ–ø–∞–¥–∞–µ–º –≤ —Ä–∞–π–æ–Ω, –≥–¥–µ –∂–∏–≤—É —è –∏ –æ—Å—Ç–∞–ª—å–Ω—ã–µ).
  • (–ö–æ–º–Ω–∞—Ç—ã –≤ –º–Ω–æ–≥–æ—ç—Ç–∞–∂–∫–µ –∑–∞–ø–æ–ª–Ω–µ–Ω—ã –∑–∞–ø–ª–∞—Ç–∞–Ω–Ω—ã–º–∏ –ø–∞–ª–∞—Ç–∫–∞–º–∏, –∏–º–ø—Ä–æ–≤–∏–∑–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞–Ω–Ω—ã–º–∏ –∫—Ä–æ–≤–∞—Ç—è–º–∏ –∏–∑ –¥–µ—Ä–µ–≤—è–Ω–Ω—ã—Ö –¥–æ—Å–æ–∫ –∏ –º–µ—Ç–∞–ª–ª–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–∏—Ö –ø—Ä—É—Ç—å–µ–≤, –∞ –Ω–µ–∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–µ –ª—é–¥–∏ –ø—Ä–æ—Å—Ç–æ —Å–ø—è—Ç –Ω–∞ —Ç–æ–ª—Å—Ç—ã—Ö –∫–∞—Ä—Ç–æ–Ω–Ω—ã—Ö –ø—Ä–æ—Å—Ç—ã–Ω—è—Ö.)
  • (–í–æ–∫—Ä—É–≥ —Ä–∞–∑–±—Ä–æ—Å–∞–Ω—ã —Ñ–æ–Ω–∞—Ä–∏ –∏ –≥–∞–∑–æ–≤—ã–µ –ª–∞–º–ø—ã. –í–æ–∑–¥—É—Ö –ø–∞—Ö–Ω–µ—Ç —Å–µ—Ä–æ–π.)
  • –•–µ–π, –≤—á–µ—Ä–∞—à–Ω–∏–π —à—Ç–æ—Ä–º —Å–Ω–æ–≤–∞ –∏—Å–ø–æ—Ä—Ç–∏–ª –¥–æ–∂–¥–µ–≤—É—é –∑–∞—â–∏—Ç—É? –ü–æ–ª –æ–ø—è—Ç—å —Å—Ç–∞–Ω–æ–≤–∏—Ç—Å—è –º–æ–∫—Ä—ã–º.
  • –ö–∞–∫–∏–º –æ–±—Ä–∞–∑–æ–º? –Ø –º–µ–Ω—è–ª –µ–≥–æ –Ω–µ–¥–µ–ª—é –Ω–∞–∑–∞–¥.
  • –¢—ã –æ–±—Ä–µ–∑–∞–ª —É–≥–ª—ã –∏–ª–∏ —Ç—ã –ø—ã—Ç–∞–µ—à—å—Å—è –æ–±–º–∞–Ω—É—Ç—å –Ω–∞—Å? –°–ª—ã—à—å, –µ—Å–ª–∏ —ç—Ç–æ –∑–¥–∞–Ω–∏–µ —Ä–∞–∑—Ä—É—à–∏—Ç—Å—è, —Ç–µ–±–µ –±—É–¥–µ—Ç –æ–π –∫–∞–∫ –Ω–µ —Å–ª–∞–¥–∫–æ!

  • –ö—É—Ä–∏—Ü—ã –≤—Å–µ –µ—â–µ –æ—Ç–∫–ª–∞–¥—ã–≤–∞—é—Ç —è–π—Ü–∞, –Ω–æ –Ω–µ –≤—Å–µ –∏–∑ –Ω–∏—Ö –ø–∏—Ç–∞—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω—ã–µ. –ë–æ–ª—å—à–∏–Ω—Å—Ç–≤–æ —è–π—Ü –∏–º–µ—é—Ç –º—è–≥–∫—É—é –æ–±–æ–ª–æ—á–∫—É.

  • (–≠—Ç–æ –°—å—é–∑–µ–Ω)
  • –ß—Ç–æ —Å –Ω–µ–π –ø—Ä–æ–∏–∑–æ—à–ª–æ?
  • (–Ø –¥–æ—Å—Ç–∞—é —Å–∫–æ–º–∫–∞–Ω–Ω—ã–π –ª–∏—Å—Ç–æ–∫ –±—É–º–∞–≥–∏ –∏ –ø—Ä–æ—Ç—è–≥–∏–≤–∞—é –µ–π).
  • (–≠—Ç–æ —Ñ–æ—Ç–æ–≥—Ä–∞—Ñ–∏—è —Å –∂–µ–Ω—â–∏–Ω–æ–π –Ω–∞ –∫—Ä–æ–≤–∞—Ç–∏, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä–∞—è –¥–µ—Ä–∂–∏—Ç –Ω–æ–≤–æ—Ä–æ–∂–¥—ë–Ω–Ω–æ–≥–æ —Ä–µ–±—ë–Ω–∫–∞.
  • –ï—ë –∑–æ–≤—É—Ç –°—å—é–∑–µ–Ω. –û–Ω–∞ –Ω–µ–¥–∞–≤–Ω–æ —Ä–æ–¥–∏–ª–∞ —Ä–µ–±–µ–Ω–∫–∞. –£ –Ω–µ–µ –º–æ–≥–ª–∞ –±—ã—Ç—å —Å—á–∞—Å—Ç–ª–∏–≤–∞—è —Å–µ–º—å—è, –Ω–æ‚Ä¶–µ—ë –º—É–∂ —É—à–µ–ª –∏ –∑–∞–±—Ä–∞–ª —Å —Å–æ–±–æ–π —Ä–µ–±–µ–Ω–∫–∞
  • –¢–µ–ø–µ—Ä—å –æ–Ω–∞..–≤–æ—Ç —Ç–∞–∫–∞—è. –í–æ—Ç —á—Ç–æ –ø—Ä–æ–∏—Å—Ö–æ–¥–∏—Ç —Å –ª—é–¥—å–º–∏, –∫–æ–≥–¥–∞ –æ–Ω–∏ –ø–æ–ø–∞–¥–∞—é—Ç –ø–æ–¥ –¥–æ–∂–¥—å. –û–Ω–∏ –Ω–∏–∫–æ–≥–¥–∞ –Ω–µ –ø—Ä–æ—Å—ã–ø–∞—é—Ç—Å—è –∏ –ø—Ä–∏—Ö–æ–¥–∏—Ç—Å—è –ø–æ–ª–∞–≥–∞—Ç—å—Å—è –Ω–∞ —ç—Ç–∏ –∞–ø–ø–∞—Ä–∞—Ç—ã.
  • –í–æ—Ç –ø–æ—á–µ–º—É —ç—Ç–∏ –∫—Ä–∞—Å–∏–≤—ã–µ –º–µ—Å—Ç–∞ –∏—Å—á–µ–∑–ª–∏. –î–æ–∂–¥—å —Å–º—ã–ª –∏—Ö‚Ä¶ –ú—ã, –∫–∞–∫ —Å–∫–æ—Ç, –∂–∏–≤–µ–º –ø–æ–¥ –∫—Ä—ã—à–∞–º–∏.
  • –ï—ë —Å–æ–Ω‚Ä¶‚Ä¶. –ø—Ä–µ–∫—Ä–∞—Å–µ–Ω‚Ä¶

**choice: **

  • –≠—Ç–æ –≤—Å–µ, —á—Ç–æ —É –Ω–∞—Å –µ—Å—Ç—å.
  • –î—É–º–∞—é —è —Å–º–æ–≥—É –ø—Ä–∏–Ω–µ—Å—Ç–∏ —á—Ç–æ-—Ç–æ –¥—Ä—É–≥–æ–µ
  • –°—é–¥–∞

1-3 ‚Äã

  • (–ü–æ—Å–ª–µ –Ω–∞—à–µ–π –ø–æ—Å–ª–µ–¥–Ω–µ–π –ø—Ä–æ–≥—É–ª–∫–∏ –æ–Ω–∞ –Ω–∞—á–∞–ª–∞ —á–∞—Å—Ç–æ –±—Ä–æ–¥–∏—Ç—å –ø–æ –æ–∫—Ä–µ—Å—Ç–Ω–æ—Å—Ç—è–º –æ–¥–Ω–∞.)
  • –Ø —Å–ª—ã—à–∞–ª–∞, –æ —á–µ–º –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏–ª–∏ –∂–∏—Ç–µ–ª–∏ –Ω–∞ –ª–µ—Å—Ç–Ω–∏—Ü–µ. –û–Ω–∏ –ø–ª–∞–Ω–∏—Ä—É—é—Ç –æ—Ç–∫–ª—é—á–∏—Ç—å –µ–π –∞–ø–ø–∞—Ä–∞—Ç –∂–∏–∑–Ω–µ–æ–±–µ—Å–ø–µ—á–µ–Ω–∏—è.
  • –û–Ω–∏ –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏–ª–∏, —á—Ç–æ –Ω–µ —Å—Ç–æ–∏—Ç —Ç—Ä–∞—Ç–∏—Ç—å —Ä–µ—Å—É—Ä—Å—ã –Ω–∞ —Ç–µ—Ö, –∫—Ç–æ —É–∂–µ –Ω–µ –ø—Ä–æ—Å–Ω–µ—Ç—Å—è.
  • –ß—Ç–æ? –ö–∞–∫ –æ–Ω–∏ —Å–º–µ—é—Ç!?
  • –î–∞–∂–µ —Ç–∞–∫, –æ–Ω–∏ –Ω–µ –º–æ–≥—É—Ç —ç—Ç–æ–≥–æ —Å–¥–µ–ª–∞—Ç—å‚Ä¶ —ç—Ç–æ —É–±–∏–π—Å—Ç–≤–æ!
  • (–ü–æ–∫–∞ —è —Ä–∞–∑–º—ã—à–ª—è–ª, –ø–µ—Ä–µ–¥–æ –º–Ω–æ–π –ø–æ—è–≤–ª—è–µ—Ç—Å—è –º–∞–ª–µ–Ω—å–∫–∞—è —Ñ–∏–≥—É—Ä–∞ –≤ –∫–∞–ø—é—à–æ–Ω–µ –ø–æ—è–≤–ª—è–µ—Ç—Å—è.)
  • –ß—Ç–æ —Ç—ã –∑–¥–µ—Å—å –¥–µ–ª–∞–µ—à—å?
  • –ß—Ç–æ —Ç—ã –∏–º–µ–µ—à—å –≤ –≤–∏–¥—É?
  • –°—å—é–∑–µ–Ω‚Ä¶ –æ–Ω–∞ –≤ –æ–ø–∞—Å–Ω–æ—Å—Ç–∏.
  • –Ø –Ω–µ –∑–Ω–∞—é –ø–æ—á–µ–º—É, –Ω–æ —è —Ö–æ—á—É —Å–ø–∞—Å—Ç–∏ –°—å—é–∑–µ–Ω.
  • –Ø –∑–Ω–∞—é.
  • –ü–æ—Ç–æ–º—É —á—Ç–æ —Ç—ã —Ö–æ—Ä–æ—à–∞—è.
  • –ß—Ç–æ‚Ä¶ —ç—Ç–æ –≤—Å–µ —á—Ç–æ –Ω—É–∂–Ω–æ —Å–¥–µ–ª–∞—Ç—å? –ù–æ –ª–µ–≥–∫–æ —Å–∫–∞–∑–∞—Ç—å, —á–µ–º —Å–¥–µ–ª–∞—Ç—å. –ú—ã –Ω–µ –º–æ–∂–µ–º –ø—Ä–æ—Å—Ç–æ –∑–∞—Å—Ç–∞–≤–∏—Ç—å –∫–æ–≥–æ-—Ç–æ —Å–∫–∞–∑–∞—Ç—å, —á—Ç–æ –æ–Ω–∞ —Ö–æ—á–µ—Ç –ø—Ä–æ—Å–Ω—É—Ç—å—Å—è.
  • –¢—ã‚Ä¶ –º–æ–∂–µ—à—å —ç—Ç–æ —Å–¥–µ–ª–∞—Ç—å?
  • –ï—Å–ª–∏ –°—å—é–∑–µ–Ω –ø—Ä–æ—Å–Ω–µ—Ç—Å—è, –æ–Ω–∞ –±—É–¥–µ—Ç –≤ –±–µ–∑–æ–ø–∞—Å–Ω–æ—Å—Ç–∏, –¥–∞?
  • –ú—ã –ø–æ–ø–∞–¥–µ–º –≤ –µ—ë —Å–æ–Ω.
  • ‚Ä¶ –ß—Ç–æ?! –ù–æ‚Ä¶ –∫–∞–∫?
  • –î–∞.
  • –ù–æ‚Ä¶ –∫–∞–∫ –º—ã —Å–ø–∞—Å–µ–º –µ—ë? –ú—ã –Ω–µ –º–æ–∂–µ–º –ø—Ä–æ—Å—Ç–æ —É–±–µ–¥–∏—Ç—å –∏—Ö –Ω–µ –¥–µ–ª–∞—Ç—å —ç—Ç–æ–≥–æ‚Ä¶
  • (–ú–µ–Ω—è —É—Å–ø–æ–∫–∞–∏–≤–∞–µ—Ç —Ç–æ, —á—Ç–æ —è —É–∂–µ —Å–∫–∞–∑–∞–ª –µ–π –Ω–µ –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç—å –Ω–∏ —Å –∫–µ–º, –Ω–æ —è –≤—Å–µ —Ä–∞–≤–Ω–æ –±–µ—Å–ø–æ–∫–æ—é—Å—å –æ —Ç–æ–º, —á—Ç–æ –µ–µ –º–æ–≥—É—Ç —Ä–∞—Å–∫—Ä—ã—Ç—å.)
  • –ù–æ‚Ä¶ –æ–Ω–∞ –≤–∏–¥–∏—Ç —Å–Ω—ã –¥—Ä—É–≥–∏—Ö –ª—é–¥–µ–π‚Ä¶ –ó–∞–≥–∞–¥–∫–∏ —ç—Ç–æ–π –¥–µ–≤—É—à–∫–∏ –ø—Ä–æ–¥–æ–ª–∂–∞—é—Ç –Ω–∞–∫–∞–ø–ª–∏–≤–∞—Ç—å—Å—è.

**choice: **

  • –¢—ã —Ö–æ—Ä–æ—à–∞—è
  • –û–Ω–∏ –Ω–µ –∏–º–µ—é—Ç –ø—Ä–∞–≤–∞!

1-4 ‚Äã

  • (–ê–ø–ø–∞—Ä–∞—Ç –∂–∏–∑–Ω–µ–æ–±–µ—Å–ø–µ—á–µ–Ω–∏—è –≤—Å–µ —Ç–∞–∫ –∂–µ —É–≤–µ—Ä–µ–Ω–Ω–æ –≥—É–¥–∏—Ç
  • (–°—å—é–∑–µ–Ω –º–∏—Ä–Ω–æ –ª–µ–∂–∏—Ç –Ω–∞ –∫—Ä–æ–≤–∞—Ç–∏; –º—ã –Ω–µ –ø–æ–∑–≤–æ–ª–∏–º –∏–º —Ä–µ—à–∏—Ç—å –µ–µ —Å—É–¥—å–±—É.)

  • –î–∞, –∞ –æ—Å—Ç–∞–ª—å–Ω–æ–µ –º–æ–∂–µ—à—å –æ—Å—Ç–∞–≤–∏—Ç—å –º–Ω–µ
  • –ö–∞–∫–∞—è —É–¥–æ–±–Ω–∞—è —Å–ø–æ—Å–æ–±–Ω–æ—Å—Ç—å‚Ä¶

  • –ï—Å–ª–∏ –º—ã –ø–æ–ª—É—á–∏–º —Ç—Ä–∞–≤–º—É —Ç–∞–º, —ç—Ç–æ –º–æ–∂–µ—Ç –æ—Ç—Ä–∞–∑–∏—Ç—å—Å—è –∏ –Ω–∞ –Ω–∞—à–∏—Ö –Ω–∞—Å—Ç–æ—è—â–∏—Ö —Ç–µ–ª–∞—Ö.

  • –í—Å–µ –≤ –ø–æ—Ä—è–¥–∫–µ. –ï—Å–ª–∏ –±—ã —è –ø–æ –∫–∞–∫–æ–π-—Ç–æ —Å—Ç—Ä–∞–Ω–Ω–æ–π –ø—Ä–∏—á–∏–Ω–µ –Ω–µ –ø—Ä–æ—Å–Ω—É–ª—Å—è –æ—Ç –¥–æ–∂–¥—è, —Ç–æ, –Ω–∞–≤–µ—Ä–Ω–æ–µ, –±—ã–ª –±—ã –∫–∞–∫ –°—å—é–∑–µ–Ω, –∏ –≤ –∫–æ–Ω—Ü–µ –∫–æ–Ω—Ü–æ–≤ –º–Ω–µ –æ—Ç–∫–ª—é—á–∏–ª–∏ –±—ã —Å–∏—Å—Ç–µ–º—É –∂–∏–∑–Ω–µ–æ–±–µ—Å–ø–µ—á–µ–Ω–∏—è.

  • (–û–Ω–∞ —Å–º–æ—Ç—Ä–∏—Ç –º–Ω–µ –≤ –≥–ª–∞–∑–∞, –µ—ë —á–∏—Å—Ç—ã–µ –≥–ª–∞–∑–∞ –∫–∞–∑–∞–ª–æ—Å—å, —á—Ç–æ –æ–Ω–∞ –≤–∏–¥–∏—Ç –º–µ–Ω—è –Ω–∞—Å–∫–≤–æ–∑—å.)
  • –ö–∞–∂–µ—Ç—Å—è —Ç—ã –≥–æ—Ç–æ–≤.
  • –î–µ—Ä–∂–∏—Å—å –∑–∞ –º–æ—é —Ä—É–∫—É
  • –•–æ—Ä–æ—à–æ.
  • (–Ø —Å—Ö–≤–∞—Ç–∏–ª –µ–µ —Ä—É–∫—É; –æ–Ω–∞ –±—ã–ª–∞ —Ö–æ–ª–æ–¥–Ω–∞—è –∫–∞–∫ –¥–æ–∂–¥—å.)
  • (–û–Ω–∞ –≤–Ω–∏–º–∞—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω–æ —Å–º–æ—Ç—Ä–∏—Ç –Ω–∞ –°—å—é–∑–µ–Ω, –ø—Ä–æ—Ç—è–≥–∏–≤–∞—è –≤—Ç–æ—Ä—É—é —Ä—É–∫—É, —á—Ç–æ–±—ã –∫–æ—Å–Ω—É—Ç—å—Å—è –µ—ë —Ç–µ–ª–∞.)
  • (–≠—Ç–æ –Ω–µ–≤–µ—Ä–æ—è—Ç–Ω–æ‚Ä¶ –í–æ–π–¥—è –≤ —á–µ–π-—Ç–æ —Å–æ–Ω –∏ –≤—Å–µ.)

**choice: **

  • –•–æ—Ä–æ—à–æ

1-5 ‚Äã

  • –≠—ç—ç‚Ä¶
  • (–ú–æ–µ –∑—Ä–µ–Ω–∏–µ –≤–Ω–µ–∑–∞–ø–Ω–æ –ø–æ—Ç–µ–º–Ω–µ–ª–æ, –∫–∞–∫ –±—É–¥—Ç–æ —á—Ç–æ-—Ç–æ –Ω–µ–ø—Ä–æ–∏–∑–≤–æ–ª—å–Ω–æ –∑–∞–∫—Ä—ã–ª–æ –º–Ω–µ –≥–ª–∞–∑–∞.)

  • (–°–æ–ª–Ω–µ—á–Ω—ã–µ –ª—É—á–∏ –ø—Ä–æ–Ω–∏–∫–∞—é—Ç –≤ –æ–∫–Ω–∞.)

  • –†–æ–±–µ—Ä—Ç, –£ –Ω–∞—Å –≥–æ—Å—Ç–∏! –ü—Ä–∏—Ö–æ–¥–∏ –∏ –ø–æ–∑–Ω–∞–∫–æ–º—å—Å—è —Å –Ω–∏–º!
  • –û—É, –ø—Ä–∏–≤–µ—Ç. –ò–∑–≤–∏–Ω—è—é—Å—å, —á—Ç–æ –Ω–µ –≤—ã—à–µ–ª –ø–æ–ø—Ä–∏–≤–µ—Ç—Å—Ç–≤–æ–≤–∞—Ç—å –≤–∞—Å —Ä–∞–Ω—å—à–µ.
  • (–û–Ω –∂–µ –¥–æ–ª–∂–µ–Ω –±—ã—Ç—å –Ω–∞ –∑–µ–º–ª–µ‚Ä¶)
  • (–£—à–µ–ª —Ä–∞–±–æ—Ç–∞—Ç—å –Ω–∞ —Å—Ç—Ä–æ–∏—Ç–µ–ª—å—Å—Ç–≤–æ –∫–∞–∫–æ–≥–æ-—Ç–æ –ø—Ä–æ–µ–∫—Ç–∞‚Ä¶)
  • –ó–¥—Ä–∞–≤—Å—Ç–≤—É–π—Ç–µ‚Ä¶

  • (–°—å—é–∑–µ–Ω —Ä–∞–∑–≤–æ—Ä–∞—á–∏–≤–∞–µ—Ç—Å—è –∏ —É—à–ª–∞ –æ–±—Ä–∞—Ç–Ω–æ –Ω–∞ –∫—É—Ö–Ω—é, –≥–¥–µ –≤ —Ä–µ–∞–ª—å–Ω–æ–º –º–∏—Ä–µ –æ–Ω–∞ –º–æ–≥–ª–∞ —Ç–æ–ª—å–∫–æ –≥–æ—Ç–æ–≤–∏—Ç—å –Ω–∞ –æ–≥–Ω–µ –∏ –≤ –º–∞–ª–µ–Ω—å–∫–æ–º –∫–æ—Ç–µ–ª–∫–µ, –∞ –∑–¥–µ—Å—å —É –Ω–µ–µ –µ—Å—Ç—å –¥—É—Ö–æ–≤–∫–∞.)
  • –û–Ω–∞ –ª—é–±–∏—Ç –≥–æ—Ç–æ–≤–∏—Ç—å –ø–µ—á–µ–Ω—å—è –∏ —É –Ω–µ–µ –æ–Ω–∏ –ø–æ–ª—É—á–∞—é—Ç—Å—è –ø—Ä–æ—Å—Ç–æ –≤–æ—Å—Ö–∏—Ç–∏—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω—ã–º–∏! –í–∞–º —Å–ª–µ–¥—É–µ—Ç —Ç–æ–∂–µ –ø–æ–ø—Ä–æ–±–æ–≤–∞—Ç—å, –µ—Å–ª–∏ –≤—ã –ª—é–±–∏—Ç–µ.
  • –ú—ã‚Ä¶–º—ã —Å —É–¥–æ–≤–æ–ª—å—Å—Ç–≤–∏–µ–º

  • –ú—ã –ø–æ–Ω–∏–º–∞–µ–º
  • (–ü–æ—Å–ª–µ —ç—Ç–æ–≥–æ, –†–æ–±–µ—Ä—Ç —É—à–µ–ª. –Ø –ø–æ–¥–æ—à–µ–ª –∫ –¥–≤–µ—Ä–∏, —á—Ç–æ–±—ã –ø–æ—Å–º–æ—Ç—Ä–µ—Ç—å, —á—Ç–æ –ø—Ä–æ–∏—Å—Ö–æ–¥–∏—Ç —Å–Ω–∞—Ä—É–∂–∏.)
  • (–ù–æ –∫–æ–≥–¥–∞ —è –ø–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∞—á–∏–≤–∞—é —Ä—É—á–∫—É, —è –ø–æ–Ω—è–ª, —á—Ç–æ —è –Ω–µ –º–æ–≥—É –æ—Ç–∫—Ä—ã—Ç—å –µ—ë. –≠—Ç–æ –±—ã–ª–∞ –æ–±—ã—á–Ω–∞—è —Å—Ç–µ–Ω–∞
  • –ù–µ –æ—Ç–∫—Ä—ã–≤–∞–µ—Ç—Å—è‚Ä¶
  • –≠—Ç–æ –¥–æ–º –≤–æ —Å–Ω–µ –°—å—é–∑–µ–Ω–∞
  • –¢–∞–∫ —á—Ç–æ‚Ä¶–ó–∞ –¥–≤–µ—Ä—å—é –Ω–∏—á–µ–≥–æ –Ω–µ—Ç‚Ä¶
  • –ü–µ—á–µ–Ω—å—è –≥–æ—Ç–æ–≤—ã! –ü—Ä–∏—Ö–æ–¥–∏—Ç–µ –∏ –ø–æ–ø—Ä–æ–±—É–π—Ç–µ!
  • (–°—å—é–∑–∞–Ω –Ω–∞–¥–µ–≤–∞–µ—Ç —Ä—É–∫–∞–≤–∏—Ü—ã –¥–ª—è –¥—É—Ö–æ–≤–∫–∏, –∞ –Ω–∞ –ø—Ä–æ—Ç–∏–≤–Ω–µ –∞–∫–∫—É—Ä–∞—Ç–Ω–æ —Ä–∞–∑–ª–æ–∂–µ–Ω–æ —Å–≤–µ–∂–µ–∏—Å–ø–µ—á–µ–Ω–Ω–æ–µ –ø–µ—á–µ–Ω—å–µ —Å –∑–æ–ª–æ—Ç–∏—Å—Ç–æ–π –ø–æ–≤–µ—Ä—Ö–Ω–æ—Å—Ç—å—é).
  • –û—É, —Å–ø–∞—Å–∏–±–æ.
  • (–Ø –±–µ—Ä—É –æ–¥–∏–Ω –∏ –ø–µ—Ä–µ–¥–∞—é –¥—Ä—É–≥–æ–π –¥–µ–≤—É—à–∫–µ, –∞ –∑–∞—Ç–µ–º –æ—Ç–∫—É—Å—ã–≤–∞—é
  • –≠—Ç–æ‚Ä¶–í–∫—É—Å–Ω–æ!
  • –°–ª–∞–¥–∫–æ‚Ä¶

  • –•–µ—Ö–µ—Ö–µ‚Ä¶–ü–æ–∂–∞–ª—É–π—Å—Ç–∞, –≤–æ–∑—å–º–∏—Ç–µ –µ—â–µ, –µ—Å–ª–∏ –≤–∞–º –ø–æ–Ω—Ä–∞–≤–∏–ª–æ—Å—å. –í–∏–¥–µ—Ç—å, –∫–∞–∫ –¥—Ä—É–≥–∏–µ –Ω–∞—Å–ª–∞–∂–¥–∞—é—Ç—Å—è –∑–∞–∫—É—Å–∫–∞–º–∏, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä—ã–µ —è –≥–æ—Ç–æ–≤–ª—é, - –ª—É—á—à–∞—è –Ω–∞–≥—Ä–∞–¥–∞ –¥–ª—è –º–µ–Ω—è.
  • (–ù–µ —É—Å–ø–µ–≤–∞—é —è –Ω–∞—á–∞—Ç—å, –∫–∞–∫ –¥–µ–≤—É—à–∫–∞ —Ä—è–¥–æ–º —Å–æ –º–Ω–æ–π —Å –Ω–µ—Ç–µ—Ä–ø–µ–Ω–∏–µ–º, –∫–∞–∫ —Ä–µ–±–µ–Ω–æ–∫, –±–µ—Ä–µ—Ç –¥—Ä—É–≥–æ–π –∫—É—Å–æ–∫).
  • (–í –∏—Ç–æ–≥–µ –º—ã –ø—Ä–æ–≤–µ–ª–∏ –Ω–æ—á—å –≤ –≥–æ—Å—Ç–µ–≤–æ–π –∫–æ–º–Ω–∞—Ç–µ –ø–æ —Ç–µ–ø–ª–æ–º—É –ø—Ä–∏–≥–ª–∞—à–µ–Ω–∏—é –†–æ–±–µ—Ä—Ç–∞ –∏ –°—å—é–∑–µ–Ω).
  • (–ö —Ç–æ–º—É –∂–µ, –∏–¥—Ç–∏ –±–æ–ª—å—à–µ –Ω–µ–∫—É–¥–∞.)

  • –ò –∑–¥–µ—Å—å –Ω–µ—Ç—É —ç—Ç–æ–≥–æ –¥–æ–∂–¥—è.

  • –ù–æ‚Ä¶ –º—ã –¥–æ–ª–∂–Ω—ã —Ä–∞–∑–±—É–¥–∏—Ç—å –µ—ë. –≠—Ç–æ —Å–æ–Ω. –≠—Ç–æ –Ω–µ—Ä–µ–∞–ª—å–Ω–æ.
  • –¢–æ–≥–¥–∞ –∑–∞–≤—Ç—Ä–∞ –º—ã —É–±–µ–¥–∏–º –µ–µ –æ—á–Ω—É—Ç—å—Å—è –æ—Ç —ç—Ç–æ–≥–æ
  • –ê–≥–∞‚Ä¶–í –ø—Ä–æ—Ç–∏–≤–Ω–æ–º —Å–ª—É—á–∞–µ –æ–Ω–∞‚Ä¶
  • (–ü–æ—è–≤–ª—è–µ—Ç—Å—è –¥—Ä—É–≥–æ–π —á–µ–ª–æ–≤–µ–∫ –∏–∑ –∫–æ–º–Ω–∞—Ç—ã, –æ—á–µ–≤–∏–¥–Ω–æ, –º—É–∂ –°—å—é–∑–µ–Ω.)

1-6 ‚Äã

  • (–°—å—é–∑–∞–Ω –≥–æ—Ç–æ–≤–∏—Ç –æ–±–µ–¥. –ü–æ—Ö–æ–∂–µ –Ω–∞ –∫–∞—Å—Ç—Ä—é–ª—é —Å —Å—É–ø–æ–º.)

  • –î–∞? –î–µ–≤–æ—á–∫–∞ –≥–æ–ª–æ–¥–Ω–∞—è? –û–±–µ–¥ –±—É–¥–µ—Ç –≥–æ—Ç–æ–≤ —Å –º–∏–Ω—É—Ç—ã –Ω–∞ –º–∏–Ω—É—Ç—É
  • –ù-–Ω–µ—Ç —è –Ω–µ –ø—Ä–æ —ç—Ç–æ‚Ä¶ –≤—ã‚Ä¶–¥-–¥–∞–π—Ç–µ –º–Ω–µ —Å–∫–∞–∑–∞—Ç—å –≤–∞–º –ø—Ä—è–º–æ. –°–ª—É—à–∞–π—Ç–µ, –º–∏—Ä –≤ –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–º –≤—ã —Å–µ–π—á–∞—Å - –Ω–µ–Ω–∞—Å—Ç–æ—è—â–∏–π. –≠—Ç–æ –≤—Å–µ —Å–æ–Ω
  • –û —á–µ–º —Ç—ã –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—à—å? –∫–∞–∫–æ–π —Å–æ–Ω, —á—Ç–æ –Ω–µ–Ω–∞—Å—Ç–æ—è—â–µ–µ?

  • –ß—Ç–æ‚Ä¶?

  • –ü—Ä–æ—à—É –ø—Ä–æ—â–µ–Ω–∏—è‚Ä¶ –ö–∞—Å—Ç—Ä—é–ª—è‚Ä¶–≤–æ—Ç-–≤–æ—Ç –∑–∞–∫–∏–ø–∏—Ç, –Ø –ø–æ–∂–∞–ª—É–π —Å—Ö–æ–∂—É –ø—Ä–æ–≤–µ—Ä—é –µ—ë.

  • ‚Ä¶
  • –ú–æ–∂–Ω–æ —è –æ–¥–æ–ª–∂—É —ç—Ç–æ —É —Ç–µ–±—è? –Ø —Ö–æ—á—É –ø–æ–≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç—å —Å –Ω–µ–π –µ—â–µ —Ä–∞–∑.
  • (–Ø –±–µ—Ä—É —Ä–∏—Å—É–Ω–æ–∫ –∏ –∏–¥—É –Ω–∞ –∫—É—Ö–Ω—é. –°—å—é–∑–µ–Ω —Å—Ç–æ–∏—Ç –≤–æ–∑–ª–µ –ø–ª–∏—Ç—ã, –ø–æ—Ç–µ—Ä—è–Ω–Ω–∞—è –≤ —Å–≤–æ–∏—Ö –º—ã—Å–ª—è—Ö.)

  • (–ï—ë –ª–∏—Ü–æ –≤—ã–≥–ª—è–¥–µ–ª–æ –∏–∑–º–æ–∂–¥–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–º, –µ—ë –≥–ª–∞–∑–∞ —Å–ª–µ–≥–∫–∞ –ø–æ–∫—Ä–∞—Å–Ω–µ–ª–∏.)

  • (‚Ä¶)
  • –°–æ–Ω‚Ä¶–∞–∞‚Ä¶
  • –Ø —Ç–∞–∫–∞—è‚Ä¶–±–µ–∑–æ—Ç–≤–µ—Ç—Å—Ç–≤–µ–Ω–Ω–∞—è –º–∞—Ç—å‚Ä¶—è –±—É–∫–≤–∞–ª—å–Ω–æ –±—Ä–æ—Å–∏–ª–∞ —Å–≤–æ–µ–≥–æ —Ä–µ–±–µ–Ω–∫–∞‚Ä¶

–°—Ä–µ–¥–∏ –Ω–∏—Ö –±—ã–ª–∏ –ø–∞–ø–∞ –∏ –º–∞–º–∞. –ò—Ö –∫–æ–∂–∞ –µ—â–µ –±–æ–ª—å—à–µ –ø–æ—Ç–µ–º–Ω–µ–ª–∞ –ø–æ–¥ –±–µ–∑–∂–∞–ª–æ—Å—Ç–Ω—ã–º–∏ –ª—É—á–∞–º–∏ —Å–æ–ª–Ω—Ü–∞

"–í–æ—Ç, –≤—ã–ø–µ–π..." –ú–∞–º–∞ —Å–Ω–æ–≤–∞ –ø—Ä–∏–Ω–µ—Å–ª–∞ –º–∏—Å–∫—É —Å –ª–µ–∫–∞—Ä—Å—Ç–≤–æ–º.

"–ù–æ..."

–í —ç—Ç–æ—Ç –º–æ–º–µ–Ω—Ç, –≤ –∫–æ–º–Ω–∞—Ç—É –≤–æ—à–µ–ª –ø–∞–ø–∞ –∏ –ø–æ–ª–æ–∂–∏–ª —Å–≤–æ—é —Ç—è–∂–µ–ª—É—é —Ä—É–∫—É –Ω–∞ –º–æ—é –≥–æ–ª–æ–≤—É. ‚Äú–ù–µ –≤–æ–ª–Ω—É–π—Å—è, –º—ã —á—Ç–æ-–Ω–∏–±—É–¥—å –ø—Ä–∏–¥—É–º–∞–µ–º. –ù–∞—à–µ–π –ª—é–±–∏–º–æ–π –¥–æ—á–µ—Ä–∏ –Ω–µ –Ω—É–∂–Ω–æ –±–µ—Å–ø–æ–∫–æ–∏—Ç—å—Å—è. –ü—Ä–æ—Å—Ç–æ –≤—ã–ø–µ–π —ç—Ç–æ –ª–µ–∫–∞—Ä—Å—Ç–≤–æ, —Ö–æ—Ä–æ—à–æ?

‚Äú–ü–∞–ø–∞, —Ç–≤–æ—é —Ä—É–∫–∏ –æ—á–µ–Ω—å –≥—Ä—É–±—ã–µ!‚Äù –Ø —É–±—Ä–∞–ª–∞ –µ–≥–æ —Ä—É–∫—É, –∂–∞–ª—É—è—Å—å.

"–•-–•–æ–Ω–æ–∫–∞?!" - –≤–æ—Å–∫–ª–∏–∫–Ω—É–ª–∞ –º–∞–º–∞, –≤ –µ—ë –≥–æ–ª–æ—Å–µ —Å–ª—ã—à–∞–ª–∞—Å—å –ø–∞–Ω–∏–∫–∞

–≠—Ç–æ –±—ã–ª–æ —Ç–æ, —á–µ–≥–æ —è –Ω–∏–∫–æ–≥–¥–∞ –Ω–µ —Ö–æ—Ç–µ–ª–∞ –≤–∏–¥–µ—Ç—å –≤ –µ–µ –≥–ª–∞–∑–∞—Ö.

–í–æ–∑–º–æ–∂–Ω–æ, –º–æ—è —É–ª—ã–±–∫–∞ —É—Å–ø–æ–∫–æ–∏–ª–∞ –∏—Ö. "...–î–∞. –¢—ã —Å–∫–æ—Ä–æ –ø–æ–ø—Ä–∞–≤–∏—à—å—Å—è".

–õ—É–Ω–Ω—ã–π —Å–≤–µ—Ç –∑–∞–ª–∏–≤–∞–ª –ø—É—Å—Ç—É—é, —á–∏—Å—Ç—É—é –∏ –±–ª–µ–¥–Ω—É—é –∑–µ–º–ª—é.

–ò–∑ –¥–∞–ª–µ–∫–æ–π –∫–æ–º–Ω–∞—Ç—ã –¥–æ–Ω–æ—Å–∏–ª–∏—Å—å –æ—Å—Ç—Ä—ã–µ, –Ω–∞–ø—Ä—è–∂–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–µ –≥–æ–ª–æ—Å–∞. –ù–∏–∫–æ–≥–¥–∞ —Ä–∞–Ω—å—à–µ —è –Ω–µ —Å–ª—ã—à–∞–ª–∞, —á—Ç–æ–±—ã –º–æ–∏ —Ä–æ–¥–∏—Ç–µ–ª–∏ –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏–ª–∏ —Ç–∞–∫ —Ä–µ–∑–∫–æ, –±—É–¥—Ç–æ –æ–Ω–∏ —Å—Å–æ—Ä–∏–ª–∏—Å—å.

‚Äú–•–º..? –û —á–µ–º?‚Äù –Ø –ø–æ–≤–µ—Ä–Ω—É–ª–∞—Å—å –∫ –Ω–∏–º, –Ω–∞–∫–ª–æ–Ω–∏–≤ —Å–≤–æ—é –≥–æ–ª–æ–≤—É.

–ü–∞–ø–∞ –æ–ø—É—Å—Ç–∏–ª—Å—è –Ω–∞ –∫–æ–ª–µ–Ω–∏ –ø–µ—Ä–µ–¥–æ –º–Ω–æ–π. "–≠—Ç–æ —Ç–æ, —á—Ç–æ –º–æ–∂–µ—à—å —Å–¥–µ–ª–∞—Ç—å —Ç–æ–ª—å–∫–æ —Ç—ã, –•–æ–Ω–æ–∫–∞. –ï—Å–ª–∏ –Ω–µ —Ö–æ—á–µ—à—å, –º—ã –Ω–µ –±—É–¥–µ–º —Ç–µ–±—è –∑–∞—Å—Ç–∞–≤–ª—è—Ç—å".

¬´–¢–æ–ª—å–∫–æ —è –º–æ–≥—É —Å–¥–µ–ª–∞—Ç—å? –ß—Ç–æ —ç—Ç–æ –º–æ–∂–µ—Ç –±—ã—Ç—å?¬ª

–ü–∞–ø–∞ –∑–∞–º—è–ª—Å—è. –ú–∞–º–∞ –ª–∞—Å–∫–æ–≤–æ –ø–æ–ª–æ–∂–∏–ª–∞ —Ä—É–∫—É –µ–º—É –Ω–∞ –ø–ª–µ—á–æ. ¬´–•–æ–Ω–æ–∫–∞, —Ç—ã –≥–æ—Ç–æ–≤–∞ —Å—Ç–∞—Ç—å –∂—Ä–∏—Ü–µ–π, —á—Ç–æ–±—ã –º–æ–ª–∏—Ç—å—Å—è –æ –¥–æ–∂–¥–µ?¬ª

"–ñ—Ä–∏—Ü–µ–π...? –ú–æ–ª–∏—Ç—å—Å—è –æ –¥–æ–∂–¥–µ...?"

"–ù–µ –ø–µ—Ä–µ–∂–∏–≤–∞–π. –ü—Ä–æ—Å—Ç–æ –ø—Ä–µ–¥—Å—Ç–∞–≤—å, —á—Ç–æ —ç—Ç–æ –∏–≥—Ä–∞ ‚Äî —Ç—ã –Ω–∞–¥–µ–Ω–µ—à—å –∫—Ä–∞—Å–∏–≤—É—é –æ–¥–µ–∂–¥—É, —Å–∫–∞–∂–µ—à—å –Ω–µ—Å–∫–æ–ª—å–∫–æ —Å–ª–æ–≤, –∏ –≤—Å–µ." - –°–∫–∞–∑–∞–ª–∞ –ª–∞—Å–∫–æ–≤–æ –º–∞–º–∞.

¬´–ú–º-—Ö–º. –û—Å—Ç–∞–ª—å–Ω–æ–µ –º—ã —Å–¥–µ–ª–∞–µ–º —Å–∞–º–∏¬ª.

¬´–Ø...–∏ –≤–ø—Ä–∞–≤–¥—É —Å–º–æ–≥—É –ø–æ–º–æ—á—å?¬ª ‚Äî —É—Ç–æ—á–Ω–∏–ª–∞ —è.

¬´–¢—ã –µ–¥–∏–Ω—Å—Ç–≤–µ–Ω–Ω–∞—è, –∫—Ç–æ –º–æ–∂–µ—Ç –ø–æ–º–æ—á—å, –•–æ–Ω–æ–∫–∞...¬ª ‚Äî –º–∞–º–∞ –ø–æ—Å–º–æ—Ç—Ä–µ–ª–∞ –Ω–∞ –º–µ–Ω—è.

¬´–ï–¥–∏–Ω—Å—Ç–≤–µ–Ω–Ω–∞—è...¬ª ‚Äî –ø—Ä–æ—à–µ–ø—Ç–∞–ª–∞ —è —Å–µ–±–µ –ø–æ–¥ –Ω–æ—Å.

–ù–∞–∫–æ–Ω–µ—Ü-—Ç–æ... —è —Å–º–æ–≥—É –ø–æ–º–æ—á—å –º–∞–º–µ –∏ –ø–∞–ø–µ! –Ø –±–æ–ª—å—à–µ –Ω–µ –±—É–¥—É –æ–±—É–∑–æ–π, –Ω–∏ –±–æ–ª—å–Ω—ã–º —Ä–µ–±–µ–Ω–∫–æ–º, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä–æ–≥–æ –æ–Ω–∏ –∂–∞–ª–µ–ª–∏. –ë—ã–ª–æ —á—Ç–æ-—Ç–æ, —á—Ç–æ –º–æ–≥–ª–∞ —Å–¥–µ–ª–∞—Ç—å —Ç–æ–ª—å–∫–æ —è.

¬´–Ø –±—É–¥—É –∂—Ä–∏—Ü–µ–π¬ª, ‚Äî —É–ª—ã–±–Ω—É–ª–∞—Å—å —è –∏–º.

‚Äú–Ø –∑–Ω–∞–ª–∞, —á—Ç–æ –æ–Ω–∞ –º–Ω–µ –ø–æ–¥–æ–π–¥–µ—Ç.‚Äù

‚Äú–•–æ–Ω–æ–∫–∞ –≤—ã—Ä–æ—Å–ª–∞ —Ç–∞–∫–æ–π –∫—Ä–∞—Å–∞–≤–∏—Ü–µ–π.‚Äù

‚Äú–ß—Ç–æ —Ç—ã –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—à—å? –Ø –∂–µ –æ–Ω–∞ –∏ –µ—Å—Ç—å!".

¬´–î–µ–π—Å—Ç–≤–∏—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω–æ. –•–æ–Ω–æ–∫–∞ —Ç–µ–ø–µ—Ä—å –Ω–∞—à–∞ –•–∞—Ä—É-–Ω–æ-–ú–∏–∫–æ (–∂—Ä–∏—Ü–∞ –≤–µ—Å–Ω—ã)¬ª, ‚Äî —Å–∫–∞–∑–∞–ª –ø–∞–ø–∞. ¬´–°–º–æ—Ç—Ä–∏ ‚Äî –≤–∏—à–Ω–µ–≤–æ–µ –¥–µ—Ä–µ–≤–æ –≤–æ –¥–≤–æ—Ä–µ –∑–∞—Ü–≤–µ–ª–æ –±–ª–∞–≥–æ–¥–∞—Ä—è —Ç–µ–±–µ¬ª.

‚Äú–ò –≤–ø—Ä–∞–≤–¥—É –∑–∞—Ü–≤–µ–ª–∏!‚Äù –†–∞–¥–æ—Å—Ç–Ω–æ –∑–∞–∫—Ä–∏—á–∞–ª–∞ —è. ‚Äú–≠—Ç–æ –≤—Å–µ –±–ª–∞–≥–æ–¥–∞—Ä—è –º–Ω–µ?‚Äù

‚Äú–î–∞. –° —Ç–æ–≥–æ –º–æ–º–µ–Ω—Ç–∞, –∫–∞–∫ —Ç—ã —Å–æ–≥–ª–∞—Å–∏–ª–∞—Å—å —Å—Ç–∞—Ç—å –•–∞—Ä—É-–Ω–æ-–ú–∏–∫–æ, –ø—Ä–æ–±—É–¥–∏–ª–∏—Å—å —Ü–≤–µ—Ç—ã‚Äù - —Å–∫–∞–∑–∞–ª –ø–∞–ø–∞.

¬´–í–µ—Ä–Ω–æ... –ü–æ—Ç–æ–º—É —á—Ç–æ —Ç—ã –±—ã–ª–∞ –∏–∑–±—Ä–∞–Ω–∞, –•–æ–Ω–æ–∫–∞¬ª, ‚Äî —Å–∫–∞–∑–∞–ª–∞ –º–∞–º–∞.

‚ÄúBut,‚Äù I said, ‚ÄúIf the gods have chosen not to send rain‚Ä¶ shouldn‚Äôt I respect their choice?‚Äù

‚ÄúHonoka‚Ä¶‚Äù

‚ÄúThey are the gods of cherry blossoms and volcanoes, aren‚Äôt they? And that volcano‚Ä¶ hasn‚Äôt it been dormant for a long time?‚Äù

Silence. The air between us grew still and heavy.

It had been nearly a year without rain. The villagers had begun to suspect the truth: that the early cherry blossoms blooming at the shrine every spring‚Ä¶ were no divine gift. Just a human-made illusion.

‚ÄúDear, maybe we should just leave the village while we still can,‚Äù Mother said nervously.

‚ÄúYou‚Äôre right. They‚Äôre probably starting to figure things out‚Ä¶‚Äù Father‚Äôs voice was tight with worry.

I‚Äôd heard lines like that before. But this time‚Ä¶ I knew things were different. Their expressions. Their postures. Their voices. The smallest of details told me everything.

I knew human emotion too well. Too deeply.

These human feelings‚Ä¶

‚ÄúHonoka,‚Äù Mother looked at me, eyes full of worry. ‚ÄúLet‚Äôs leave the village tonight. Go somewhere far away, okay?‚Äù

‚Äú‚Ä¶We‚Äôre finally leaving?‚Äù I asked.

‚ÄúYes.‚Äù

‚ÄúThen who will speak for the gods after that?‚Äù

Mother reached out and caressed my face. Softly, she said, ‚ÄúNone of it was ever real, Honoka. It was all a lie.‚Äù

‚ÄúThen you can leave.‚Äù I said.

She froze. As if the words I spoke weren‚Äôt what she expected. Or perhaps‚Ä¶ she had feared this answer, but never thought it would truly come.

‚ÄúI‚Äôll offer a dance. A prayer‚Äîthe most sincere I‚Äôve ever given. Just one rain. If the gods chose me to be their voice, then I‚Äôll do what I must.‚Äù

‚ÄúHonoka‚Ä¶‚Äù ‚Äú‚Ä¶Dear,‚Äù Father said behind her. ‚ÄúNo matter what happens, I‚Äôll go pack right now.‚ÄùI heard his footsteps rushing away.

Paper can‚Äôt wrap fire.

Especially not here‚Äîin a shrine built to worship fire itself.

So what is there left to ask for‚Ä¶ in the way of rain?





The rain‚Ä¶ was mine.

It had nothing to do with the gods who once ruled this place.

Once I understood that, I finally knew what I was.

I finally understood‚Äîwho I really was.





I was never just a shrine maiden. That night, a flickering light glowed outside the gate while chaotic voices rose. I knew then‚Äîthere wasn‚Äôt much time left for my parents to run.

Mother didn‚Äôt call for Father. She simply stumbled to the gate, her trembling fingers barely parting it a crack. The gate was immediately forced wide open. Villagers flooded into our yard, holding torches and farming tools high above their heads.

‚ÄúShrine Maiden! You owe us an explanation tonight!‚Äù

‚ÄúWe‚Äôve offered so much stuff!‚Äù

‚ÄúIf you don‚Äôt give us an answer that satisfy us, we‚Äôll burn your house down to the ground!‚Äù

Their eyes were filled with hatred.

‚ÄúYou insolent fools! Do you mean to rebel against the god?!‚Äù I rose to my feet, voice sharp and furious.

‚ÄúAll we want is a truth! We gave so much! Not a single coin fewer than required, what came in return?! You told us that the rain would come! Sure, it did rain a bit before, how come not a single drop this year?!‚Äù

‚ÄúI‚Äôve already conveyed the god‚Äôs will. The rain will be given at a proper timing.‚Äù

‚ÄúAnd we‚Äôre just supposed to believe that?! Every year, only your cherry trees bloom! Why won‚Äôt the god bless the rest of us?!‚Äù

‚ÄúPerhaps you should reflect on your own lack of devotion.‚Äù How laughable. They probably didn‚Äôt even got to know which god they were praying to. ‚ÄúOr are you intended to question the god? The one who blessed this land?‚Äù

‚ÄúThe one who shit on this land! We just want results that we can actually see and touch! Each of us is now deadly starving, these so-called gods‚Äîthey‚Äôre just a scam! A lie! And you‚Äôre all liars! Give us back everything we offered!‚Äù

‚ÄúHow a wishful thinking! ‚Äî"

A stone sliced across my cheek.

A flash of pain bloomed. One of them had thrown it. I clutched my bleeding face, scanning the crowd with a glare of fire.

Mother rushed to me in a panic, pulling me into a tight embrace.

‚ÄúYou all stop it!‚Äù she screamed, ‚ÄúHonoka did nothing wrong! It was us... We lied to her!!‚Äù Her voice was breaking with tears.

I bit my lips. Slowly, I pushed her away.

‚ÄúA lie...? She‚Äôs never a shrine maiden?!‚Äù

‚Äú...Yes, I told her she was Haru-no-Miko, that she could bless everyone... All these years, it was never...‚Äù

‚ÄúLi‚Ä¶ Liar! You deceived all of us!‚Äù

‚ÄúIt‚Äôs not her fault! I beg all of you, you can do anything to me, just... please, spare my daughter‚Ä¶‚Äù

Mother fell to her knees, clinging to me, sobbing.

If I had never agreed to be the shrine maiden... Would none of this have happened?

But if I had not agreed, I would never have realized I could bring the rain.





Just one rain. What‚Äôs so substantial.

Thick clouds devoured the lonely moon.

‚ÄúSilence!‚Äù I roared. ‚ÄúThis is the sacred Asagi shrine, a lineage blessed by the god for generations! Your defilement is a sin beyond forgiveness. The sky shall judge you!‚Äù

But my voice no longer held deterrence. The chaos only grew louder. They rushed forward with weapons raised.

I stood my ground. Why should I be afraid? I had never feared them.

Not since the day I chose to become a shrine maiden. I never feared.

Because I need to fear nothing.





As I said before: I was never a shrine maiden.













I, am the God.













‚ÄúThen‚Ä¶ let me pray for every single beings of you. I‚Äôll pray for the rain you crave so desperately.‚Äù









A cold droplet touched my instep. But it wasn‚Äôt Mother‚Äôs tears.

I did not realize what has happened back at that moment, even though I had been thinking about it with every fiber of my being.

Slowly, in front of the stunned, motionless crowd, I bent down, dipped my fingers in it, tasted it. Filled with sweetness. It was water.

Rainwater.

I really was the God who brought this rain.

A deathly stillness fell‚Äîlike a divine force had frozen every being in place.

Until I stood again, arms wide, watched those villagers with a cold smile on my face.

And next, they lifted their faces, blankly staring into the night sky.

As if answering my call‚Äîthe skies opened. Here comes the downpour. All torches were snuffed out in an instant.

Clothes soaked through their clothes, washing away the dry mud. Drop after drop, endlessly falling.

‚ÄúIt‚Äôs rain!! It‚Äôs raining!!‚Äù They cried out in bliss. They danced in the water-filled mud, cheering in the downpour.

‚ÄúShe‚Ä¶ She is the real Haru-no-Miko!! The god has answered!! The god has answered!!!‚Äù They shouted with utmost joy.

Just moments ago, they had threatened to burn down my home, to harm me and my parents. Now they knelt before me again, offering reverence, calling me the shrine maiden once more.

Fools. Pitiful fools.

However, there‚Äôs no need for me to tell them that I was the God.

Because‚Äîit‚Äôs not at all necessary.





‚ÄúMother, have you seen it? When did you tell which lie at all?‚Äù

I was yet to understand why she averted her eyes.

Was it due to shame?





Doesn‚Äôt matter.

To my parents. To these ignorant people.

For I was a god, I owe no one explanation.





During those days, even the fact that this rain never stopped again, was interpreted by me as my divine rage.





Rain, unstopping.

It was as if the rain meant to repay the drought.

Floods drowned the seeds and crops.

Water filled the cracked earth, spilled over, surged into floods. It tore down fences and swept away houses.

‚ÄúAll the sprouts we worked so hard to grow are gone! Our food stores were also ruined!!‚Äù

‚ÄúShrine Maiden! Please‚Äîdo something!!‚Äù They came to me again. Pleading.

‚ÄúThis is the blessing from god,‚Äù I answered. ‚ÄúYou must not reject it.‚Äù

‚ÄúMy house is under water! What kind of blessing is this, could your ‚Äògod‚Äô give an explanation?!‚Äù

‚ÄúI shall plead with the gods,‚Äù I said. ‚ÄúWait quietly.‚Äù

They had begged me for rain. And now, when it really came‚Äîthey begged me to make it stop instead. Absurd.

I raised the gohei and began the ritual, as I had done so many times before. Just seeing me do the ceremony always seemed to calm them.

They stood without talking. Watching.

Days went by. Nothing changed.

The patter of raindrops drowned all other sounds out. It was like the sound of my unrelenting rage.

Ridiculous. How could my own rage escape my control?





‚Ä¶Or so I told myself.



The torches would no longer catch fire.

But farming tools were mostly forged from metal.

Lately, things had only grown worse. The rain showed no sign of stopping. Some who were caught in it had collapsed, slipping into unconsciousness. They tried everything to wake them, but nothing worked.

As if their lives had quietly been taken away.

As if this rain was drawing life from them to feed the cherry blossoms.

The cherry trees had finally blossomed. They were late, but now they blanketed the mountains. The rain tapped against the delicate petals. Another villager fell. This rain was giving life, but it took away the purpose of it.

Those who touched the rain vanished like scattered cherry petals. It was not quite death in the usual sense, but with trivial differences.

Because next spring will arrive on time. But this spring, this very spring, would truly come to an ending.

Terrified, they gathered in our courtyard, begging me to stop the rain.

‚ÄúThis must be for our disrespect toward the gods!!‚Äù

‚ÄúMy husband was soaked and never woke up! This rain must be divine punishment!!‚Äù

‚ÄúPlease, Shrine Maiden! Beg the god‚Äôs mercy to stop this rain!!‚Äù

Driven by panic, the villagers flooded into my house. Even though they, too, had gotten wet from the rain.

Even though they, too, had no escape.

Father and Mother tried to block them out, but two mortal beings could not stop a full crowd.

Nearly the entire village had gathered in our yard.

They surrounded me, knelt down, clinging to my legs, begging.

Mother once held my legs that same way.

I‚Äôd had enough of them. When I met their wishes, they worshipped me. The moment I failed them, they cursed me, turned on me. There was nothing left in them worth saving.

I looked at them serenely, unmoved by their grief. ‚ÄúThis is my wrath. Your retribution,‚Äù I said.

‚ÄúWh...what...?‚Äù they stared at me, stunned.

I wanted to care no more and turned to leave.

‚Äú...You‚Ä¶ you‚Äôre not a shrine maiden at all! You‚Äôre a heretic! A cursed child after all! We‚Äôll offer you to the true god and end their rage!!‚Äù Someone among them shouted out to me.

At once, the others followed. They grabbed at me. Tore my clothes. Screamed of sacrifice.

I gave it a laugh.

‚ÄúThat‚Äôs right. I was never a shrine maiden.‚Äù I opened my arms, as I had when this rain first began. I embraced their curses. Embraced the warm, freezing rain, ‚ÄúI am Asagi Honoka. I am the God of rain.‚Äù

That was the moment the riot began. Just like that previous night.

They meant to kill me. Father and Mother swung extinguished torches, trying to hold them back.

‚ÄúIgnorant fools. Kill me so this land will never see rain again. You all will face eternal drought. The crops will die. The blossoms will wither. All life will fall! Have you thought twice before doing so?‚Äù

‚ÄúWhat a load of nonsense, kill her! She‚Äôs gone nothing but insane!‚Äù

‚ÄúShe uses those arms for rituals‚Äîcut off her hands first!!‚Äù

In the chaos, a pitchfork struck my abdomen. My brow tightened while the pain bloomed sharp.

‚ÄúLowly mortals... do you even grasp the sin you have committed?!‚Äù Still, I did not lower my arms. Such small pain could be endured. I am a God, my death would bring only ruin.

And that was enough. I longed to see the rain flood them all. Even if it comes with the fall of my deity.

But right at that next moment... From my side, a sudden force struck me.

That force went far greater than the mob. I couldn‚Äôt tell what emotion it carried. I hadn‚Äôt wasted my time understanding human feelings for a long time.

‚ÄúRun! Honoka!‚Äù

Before I stumbled backward, I caught a glimpse through the villagers to distinguish the source of that push.

It was my mother.

The next second, she died before my eyes.

Maybe the pain in my stomach had finally broken through the mask of adrenaline, or maybe it was simply the rainwater being too cold. But something inside me broke through.

And I remembered how to cry. I didn‚Äôt know why I cried. There was nothing left to cry for.

My body moved anyway, driven by instinct alone. Step by step, I fled toward the inner shrine. There‚Ä¶if I could make it past the back door, into the forest, no one would be able to follow me there.

Blood still poured from my abdomen, painting a deep red trail across the road, the stairs, the floor.

"This is the price we called down upon ourselves. Honoka, for a time, we lived better than most. But still... I regret not giving you a future worthy of you."

Beneath the villagers‚Äô attacks, Father struck a match in silence. He tossed it into the pile of kindling prepared long ago. Even in the rain, the flames bloomed, slowly consumed the shrine.

We had already faced doubt and torches‚Äîand now it was our own hands that burned away the past we obtained.





I had lost count of how many times I fell to the ground. My shrine maiden‚Äôs robes were torn to ribbons by branches and stone. The bleeding from my abdomen wouldn‚Äôt stop. It spilled into the land, mingling with the rainwater. Pale pink ripples spread across the puddles.

Within those ripples, I ignored the mud clinging to my body, trying to wipe the rain away from my vision. I kept fleeing forward, though my feet no longer knew straight lines.

The rain struck without mercy. The wounds hurt so much. I had scraped and gashed myself too many times. My strength was leaving me.

And before long, I realized that the blur in my vision wasn‚Äôt caused by rain alone. It was my mind unable to support my body. What little energy I had left. I supposed that the drowsiness carried by this rain was affecting me without distinction. Under both pressures, there was not much time left for me.

It was then I leaned against a cherry tree.

Slowly, I lifted my gaze. On branches that had once stood bare, fragile pink petals now bloomed. Its beauty stole my breath.

They were real petals.

Nobody crafted any lie.

No one suffered any sorrowness.

As lovely as they were short-lived. Just like the reflection of my whole life.

I had always loved the rain. Even as a child, I loved the rain most of all.

And yet, I had been given so few chances to meet its season.

Now, I have more rain than I could ever wish for.





So that was it... The young girl I used to be truly did love the rain.

I nearly forgot about it.





It‚Äôs cold.

And yet how warm it was. How warm the rainwater was.

In this moment, I danced beneath the rain.

Even in this fragile body, my arms still raised the gohei. I had brought it all this way. That alone surprised me.

Pink petals drifted with the light rain, falling, fading. Amid their gentle descent, I offered my final dance. What a splendid celebration it was.

If this was to be the last bloom, I would accept it‚Äîwith grace.

I knew every single tiny step of the ritual. Though I fell again and again, I rose each time, keeping the dance flowing within me.

This dance was mine alone. My last offering to the God.





All the words of mortals... will be woven into a melody of rain.

Reflecting in pale-red ripples, remains the pipe dream of a girl named ‚ÄúAsagi Honoka‚Äù.





Within this momentary spring, petals circling me like drifting ghosts. I stepped through the last movements of my ritual prayer.

I raised my hands skyward, as if to hold onto something.

‚ÄîBeneath the cherry blossoms, a divine dance of elegance and grandeur.









































‚ÄúMmm...‚Äù

‚ÄúBad dream?‚Äù

From a tattered bed among crumbling ruins, the white-haired girl stirred from sleep.

‚ÄúI do not really recall the content,‚Äù she was expressionless like usual, ‚ÄúJust... I think there were flowers.‚Äù

‚ÄúSounds like a good dream instead.‚Äù

‚ÄúA good one?... I‚Äôm yet to understand them.‚Äù Outside the window, the rain whispered down in sparse, gentle drops. ‚ÄúAnd the flowers... they were pretty.‚Äù

‚ÄúShall we try growing some flowers, too?‚Äù

‚ÄúGrow flowers?‚Äù

‚ÄúThere‚Äôs no one else traveling with us anyway. We could gather seeds, see if we can bring back flowers that are almost gone from this world.‚Äù

The girl gave a slow, uncertain nod.

‚ÄúI will try.‚Äù

–ú–æ–∂–µ—Ç, –∫—Ç–æ-–Ω–∏–±—É–¥—å –ø–æ–¥—Å–∫–∞–∂–µ—Ç, —á—Ç–æ –º–Ω–µ —Å–µ–π—á–∞—Å –¥–µ–ª–∞—Ç—å? ‚Ä¶–í—Å–µ –æ—Ç–≤–µ—Ç—Å—Ç–≤–µ–Ω–Ω–æ—Å—Ç—å –ª–æ–∂–∏—Ç—Å—è –Ω–∞ –º–µ–Ω—è.

–õ–∏—Ñ—Ç –Ω–µ —Ä–∞–±–æ—Ç–∞–µ—Ç —É–∂–µ –±–æ–≥ –∑–Ω–∞–µ—Ç —Å–∫–æ–ª—å–∫–æ –≤—Ä–µ–º–µ–Ω–∏. –°–≤—è–∑—å –º–µ–∂–¥—É –≤–æ—Å—Ç–æ—á–Ω—ã–º –∏ –∑–∞–ø–∞–¥–Ω—ã–º –∫—Ä—ã–ª—å—è–º–∏ —Ç—Ä–∞–Ω—Å–ø–æ—Ä—Ç–Ω–æ–π –∑–æ–Ω—ã –±—ã–ª–∞ –ø–æ–ª–Ω–æ—Å—Ç—å—é –∑–∞–±–ª–æ–∫–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞–Ω–∞ –Ω–∞–º–∏, —á—Ç–æ, –ø–æ–ª–∞–≥–∞—é, —Ö–æ—Ä–æ—à–æ.





–ü—É—Ç—å –∫ –ª–µ—Å—Ç–Ω–∏—Ü–µ –ø–æ–ª–Ω–æ—Å—Ç—å—é —Ä–∞–∑—Ä—É—à–∏—Ç—Å—è –æ—Ç –¥–∞–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∏—è –≤–æ–¥—ã –ø—Ä–∏–º–µ—Ä–Ω–æ —á–µ—Ä–µ–∑ 3 —á–∞—Å–∞. –ö —Ç–æ–º—É –≤—Ä–µ–º–µ–Ω–∏ —è –±—É–¥—É –ø–æ–ª–Ω–æ—Å—Ç—å—é –∑–∞–ø–µ—Ä—Ç –≤ —Ç—Ä–∞–Ω—Å–ø–æ—Ä—Ç–Ω–æ–π –∑–æ–Ω–µ.

–ù–µ –∑–Ω–∞—é, –µ—Å—Ç—å –ª–∏ —Å–º—ã—Å–ª –∑–∞–ø–∏—Å—ã–≤–∞—Ç—å —ç—Ç–æ. –ù–∏–∫—Ç–æ –Ω–µ –ø—Ä–æ—á–∏—Ç–∞–µ—Ç —ç—Ç–∏ —Å–æ–æ–±—â–µ–Ω–∏—è. –ù–∏ –æ–¥–Ω–æ –∂–∏–≤–æ–µ —Å—É—â–µ—Å—Ç–≤–æ –Ω–µ –º–æ–≥–ª–æ –±—ã –ø–µ—Ä–µ–∂–∏—Ç—å —Ç–∞–∫–æ–π —Å–∏–ª—å–Ω—ã–π –¥–æ–∂–¥—å.

–≠—Ç–æ —É–±–µ–∂–∏—â–µ —Ä–∞–Ω–æ –∏–ª–∏ –ø–æ–∑–¥–Ω–æ –∑–∞—Ç–æ–Ω–µ—Ç. –ú—ã –æ–±—Ä–µ—á–µ–Ω—ã.

–Ø –æ—á–µ–Ω—å –Ω–µ —Ö–æ—á—É —É–º–∏—Ä–∞—Ç—å –≤–æ—Ç —Ç–∞–∫. –ó–∞–ø–∏—Å—å, –¥–µ–Ω—å 305





–Ø –≤—Å–µ –µ—â–µ –Ω–∞—Ö–æ–∂—É—Å—å –≤ –ø—Ä–æ–º—ã—à–ª–µ–Ω–Ω–æ-–ø—Ä–æ–∏–∑–≤–æ–¥—Å—Ç–≤–µ–Ω–Ω–æ–π —Å–µ–∫—Ü–∏–∏ –° —ç—Ç–æ–≥–æ —É–±–µ–∂–∏—â–∞. –ü—Ä–æ—à–ª–æ —É–∂–µ 4 –¥–Ω—è —Å —Ç–µ—Ö –ø–æ—Ä, –∫–∞–∫ —à–ª—é–∑, —Å–æ–µ–¥–∏–Ω—è—é—â–∏–π —Å–µ–∫—Ü–∏—é B, –Ω–µ–æ–∂–∏–¥–∞–Ω–Ω–æ –∑–∞–∫—Ä—ã–ª—Å—è –∏–∑-–∑–∞ —Å–∏—Å—Ç–µ–º–Ω—ã—Ö –æ—à–∏–±–æ–∫.

–ù–∏–∫—Ç–æ –Ω–µ –∑–Ω–∞–µ—Ç, —á—Ç–æ –∏–º–µ–Ω–Ω–æ –Ω–µ —Ç–∞–∫ —Å —Å–∏—Å—Ç–µ–º–æ–π - –æ—Ç–≤–µ—Ç–æ–≤ –ø–æ–∫–∞ –Ω–µ—Ç. –í –ª—é–±–æ–º —Å–ª—É—á–∞–µ, —Ç–æ—Ç —Ñ–∞–∫—Ç, —á—Ç–æ –Ω–∏–∫—Ç–æ –Ω–µ –ø—ã—Ç–∞–ª—Å—è –æ—Ç–∫—Ä—ã—Ç—å –¥–≤–µ—Ä—å —Å–Ω–∞—Ä—É–∂–∏ –≤ —Ç–µ—á–µ–Ω–∏–µ —Å—Ç–æ–ª—å–∫–∏—Ö –¥–Ω–µ–π, –≥–æ–≤–æ—Ä–∏—Ç –æ —Ç–æ–º, —á—Ç–æ –ª—é–¥–∏ –∑–∞ –ø—Ä–µ–¥–µ–ª–∞–º–∏ —Å–µ–∫—Ü–∏–∏ C —Ç–æ–∂–µ —Å—Ç–æ–ª–∫–Ω—É–ª–∏—Å—å —Å —Ç—Ä—É–¥–Ω–æ—Å—Ç—è–º–∏.

–†–µ–º–æ–Ω—Ç–Ω–∏–∫–∏ –≤—Å–µ –µ—â–µ –ø—ã—Ç–∞—é—Ç—Å—è —É—Å—Ç–∞–Ω–æ–≤–∏—Ç—å —Å–≤—è–∑—å —Å –¥–∏—Å–ø–µ—Ç—á–µ—Ä—Å–∫–æ–π –ø—Ä–æ–º—ã—à–ª–µ–Ω–Ω–æ–π –∑–æ–Ω–æ–π. –í –Ω–∞—Å—Ç–æ—è—â–µ–µ –≤—Ä–µ–º—è —Å–µ–∫—Ü–∏—è C –Ω–∞—Ö–æ–¥–∏—Ç—Å—è –≤ –∏–∑–æ–ª–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞–Ω–Ω–æ–º —Å–æ—Å—Ç–æ—è–Ω–∏–∏.

–ú—ã –∑–Ω–∞–µ–º, —á—Ç–æ —à–ª—é–∑ –æ—Ç–∫—Ä—ã—Ç—å –Ω–µ–≤–æ–∑–º–æ–∂–Ω–æ. –¢–µ–º –Ω–µ –º–µ–Ω–µ–µ, –∫–∞–∂–¥—ã–π –¥–µ–Ω—å –Ω–µ—É—Ç–æ–º–∏–º—ã–µ –º–æ–ª–æ–¥—ã–µ –ª—é–¥–∏ –≤–æ–∑—è—Ç—Å—è —Å –º–µ—Ç–∞–ª–ª–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–æ–π –¥–≤–µ—Ä—å—é, –ø—ã—Ç–∞—è—Å—å –µ–µ —Å–ª–æ–º–∞—Ç—å.

–ù–æ –∫–∞–∫ –±—ã —Ç–æ –Ω–∏ –±—ã–ª–æ, –¥–∞–∂–µ –≤–∑—Ä—ã–≤—á–∞—Ç–∫–∞ –Ω–µ —Å–º–æ–∂–µ—Ç –æ—Ç–∫—Ä—ã—Ç—å –¥–≤–µ—Ä—å.





–î–ú –ø–ª–∞–Ω–∏—Ä—É–µ—Ç –∑–∞–º–∞–Ω–∏—Ç—å –Ω–∞—Å –≤ –ª–æ–≤—É—à–∫—É? –ó–∞—á–µ–º? –ú—ã –Ω–µ –º–æ–∂–µ–º –ø–æ–Ω—è—Ç—å –µ–≥–æ –ª–æ–≥–∏–∫—É, –∏ –¥–∞–∂–µ –µ—Å–ª–∏ –Ω–∞–º —É–¥–∞—Å—Ç—Å—è –µ–µ –ø–æ–Ω—è—Ç—å, –≤ –Ω–µ–µ —Ç—Ä—É–¥–Ω–æ –±—É–¥–µ—Ç –ø–æ–≤–µ—Ä–∏—Ç—å.

–ü–æ –∫—Ä–∞–π–Ω–µ–π –º–µ—Ä–µ, –º—ã –ø—ã—Ç–∞–µ–º—Å—è –ø–æ–Ω—è—Ç—å.





–†–µ–∑—É–ª—å—Ç–∞—Ç —ç—Ç–∏—Ö –ø–æ–ø—ã—Ç–æ–∫ –ø–æ–∫–∞ —Ç—â–µ—Ç–µ–Ω.





–ö–∞–∫ –±—ã —Ç–æ –Ω–∏ –±—ã–ª–æ, –Ω–∞–º, –æ–±–∏—Ç–∞—Ç–µ–ª—è–º —Å–µ–∫—Ü–∏–∏ –°, —Å–µ–π—á–∞—Å –Ω–µ –≥—Ä–æ–∑–∏—Ç –Ω–∏–∫–∞–∫–∞—è –Ω–µ–ø–æ—Å—Ä–µ–¥—Å—Ç–≤–µ–Ω–Ω–∞—è –æ–ø–∞—Å–Ω–æ—Å—Ç—å. –ó–∞–ø–∞—Å—ã –ø—Ä–æ–¥–æ–≤–æ–ª—å—Å—Ç–≤–∏—è –≤–µ–ª–∏–∫–∏, –∞ —á–∏—Å—Ç–æ–π –≤–æ–¥—ã –µ—â–µ –¥–æ—Å—Ç–∞—Ç–æ—á–Ω–æ. –ü—Ä–æ–¥–µ—Ä–∂–∞—Ç—å—Å—è –∑–¥–µ—Å—å 21 –¥–µ–Ω—å –Ω–µ —Å–æ—Å—Ç–∞–≤–∏—Ç —Ç—Ä—É–¥–∞. –ó–∞ –∏—Å–∫–ª—é—á–µ–Ω–∏–µ–º, –ø–æ–∂–∞–ª—É–π, —Ç—Ä—É–¥–Ω–æ—Å—Ç–µ–π —Å–æ —Å–Ω–æ–º –ø–æ –Ω–æ—á–∞–º.





–û–¥–Ω–∞–∫–æ —Ç–µ–º–ø–µ—Ä–∞—Ç—É—Ä–∞ –≤ –∫–æ–º–Ω–∞—Ç–µ –≤ —Å–µ–∫—Ü–∏–∏ –° –ø–æ–≤—ã—à–∞–µ—Ç—Å—è. –í—Å–µ–≥–æ –∑–∞ 4 –¥–Ω—è, —á—Ç–æ —è –∑–¥–µ—Å—å –∑–∞—Å—Ç—Ä—è–ª, —Ç–µ—Ä–º–æ—Å—Ç–∞—Ç —Å–¥–≤–∏–Ω—É–ª—Å—è –Ω–∞ 2,5‚Ñâ –æ—Ç –ø–µ—Ä–≤–æ–Ω–∞—á–∞–ª—å–Ω–æ–π –Ω–∞—Å—Ç—Ä–æ–π–∫–∏. –ü–æ—Ö–æ–∂–µ, –ø—Ä–æ–±–ª–µ–º–∞ DM –Ω–µ —Ç–æ–ª—å–∫–æ –≤ —à–ª—é–∑–µ¬∑ –ó–∞–ø–∏—Å—å: –î–µ–Ω—å 308





–®–∞—Ä–ª–∏–Ω —Å–µ–≥–æ–¥–Ω—è —Ä–∞–Ω—å—à–µ —Å–æ–æ–±—â–∏–ª–∞ –æ —Å—Ç–∞—Ç—É—Å–µ —Ç—Ä—É–±–æ–ø—Ä–æ–≤–æ–¥–Ω–æ–π —Å–µ—Ç–∏. –ò–∑ —Ç—Ä—É–± –±–æ–ª—å—à–µ –Ω–µ –¥–æ–Ω–æ—Å–∏—Ç—Å—è –Ω–∏ –∑–≤—É–∫–∞, –∞ –≤–æ–¥–æ–º–µ—Ä–∫–∞ –¥–∞–≤–Ω–æ –Ω–µ –¥–≤–∏–≥–∞–µ—Ç—Å—è.

–í–æ–∑–º–æ–∂–Ω–æ, —ç—Ç–æ –æ–∑–Ω–∞—á–∞–µ—Ç, —á—Ç–æ –¥–æ–∂–¥–µ–≤–∞—è –≤–æ–¥–∞, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä–∞—è –¥–æ–ª–∂–Ω–∞ —Ç–µ—á—å —á–µ—Ä–µ–∑ —Å–µ–∫—Ü–∏—é C, –æ—Å—Ç–∞–Ω–æ–≤–∏–ª–∞—Å—å. –ú—ã –Ω–µ —É–≤–µ—Ä–µ–Ω—ã, —á—Ç–æ —ç—Ç–æ –∏–∑-–∑–∞ —Ç–æ–≥–æ, —á—Ç–æ –Ω–∞ —É–ª–∏—Ü–µ –æ—Å—Ç–∞–Ω–æ–≤–∏–ª—Å—è –¥–æ–∂–¥—å..–∏–ª–∏ –∏–∑-–∑–∞ –ø—Ä–æ–±–ª–µ–º —Å —Ç—Ä—É–±–æ–ø—Ä–æ–≤–æ–¥–Ω–æ–π —Å–∏—Å—Ç–µ–º–æ–π.





–ö–æ–Ω–µ—á–Ω–æ, –º—ã –Ω–µ –Ω–∞–¥–µ–µ–º—Å—è –Ω–∞ –ø–æ—Å–ª–µ–¥–Ω–µ–µ, –Ω–æ –º—ã —Ç–∞–∫–∂–µ –Ω–µ —É–≤–µ—Ä–µ–Ω—ã, —á—Ç–æ —Å—Ç–æ–∏—Ç –ø—Ä–∞–∑–¥–Ω–æ–≤–∞—Ç—å. –ü–æ –∫—Ä–∞–π–Ω–µ–π –º–µ—Ä–µ, —è –Ω–µ –≥–æ—Ç–æ–≤ –∫ –ø–µ—Ä–µ–º–µ–Ω–∞–º —Ç–∞–∫ —Å–∫–æ—Ä–æ‚Ä¶–ø–æ–∫–∞.





–°–µ–∫—Ü–∏—è –° –≤—Å–µ –µ—â–µ –≤ –∏–∑–æ–ª—è—Ü–∏–∏. –®–ª—é–∑ –æ—Å—Ç–∞–µ—Ç—Å—è –Ω–µ–ø–æ–≤—Ä–µ–∂–¥–µ–Ω–Ω—ã–º, –∏ –¥–∞–∂–µ –Ω–∞—à–µ —Å–∞–º–æ–µ —Å–æ–≤–µ—Ä—à–µ–Ω–Ω–æ–µ –æ–±–æ—Ä—É–¥–æ–≤–∞–Ω–∏–µ —Å–ø–æ—Å–æ–±–Ω–æ —Å—á–∏—Å—Ç–∏—Ç—å –ª–∏—à—å —Ç–æ–Ω–∫–∏–π —Å–ª–æ–π –º–µ—Ç–∞–ª–ª–∏—á–µ—Å–∫–∏—Ö –æ–±–ª–æ–º–∫–æ–≤ —Å —ç—Ç–æ–π –¥–≤–µ—Ä–∏.

–ß—Ç–æ –Ω–µ —Ç–∞–∫ —Å –î–ú? –ß—Ç–æ –∏–º–µ–Ω–Ω–æ —Å–µ–π—á–∞—Å –ø—Ä–æ–∏—Å—Ö–æ–¥–∏—Ç —Å–Ω–∞—Ä—É–∂–∏? –ü–æ—á–µ–º—É –Ω–µ –ø—Ä–∏—Ö–æ–¥—è—Ç —Å–ø–∞—Å–∞—Ç–µ–ª–∏?

–ö —Å—á–∞—Å—Ç—å—é, –∫–æ–º–Ω–∞—Ç–Ω–∞—è —Ç–µ–º–ø–µ—Ä–∞—Ç—É—Ä–∞ –ø–µ—Ä–µ—Å—Ç–∞–ª–∞ –ø–æ–¥–Ω–∏–º–∞—Ç—å—Å—è –ø–æ—Å–ª–µ 5 –≥—Ä–∞–¥—É—Å–æ–≤ –ø–æ –§–∞—Ä–µ–Ω–≥–µ–π—Ç—É. –ú–Ω–µ –Ω–µ —á—É–≤—Å—Ç–≤—É—é —Ç–∞–∫—É—é –∂–∞—Ä—É, –ø–æ—Å–ª–µ —Å–Ω—è—Ç–∏—è –∫—É—Ä—Ç–∫–∏.





–°–µ–≥–æ–¥–Ω—è, –ò–∞—Ñ–µ—Ç –≤–º–µ—Å—Ç–µ —Å —Ç—Ä–µ–º—è –Ω–∞—à–∏–º–∏ –ª—é–¥—å–º–∏ –æ—Ç–ø—Ä–∞–≤–∏–ª—Å—è –∏—Å—Å–ª–µ–¥–æ–≤–∞—Ç—å —Å–±–æ—Ä–æ—á–Ω—É—é –ª–∏–Ω–∏—é. –ï—Å–ª–∏ –∏–º —É–¥–∞—Å—Ç—Å—è —É—Å–ø–µ—à–Ω–æ –æ—Ç–∫–ª—é—á–∏—Ç—å –∫–æ–Ω–≤–µ–π–µ—Ä—ã –≤–Ω—É—Ç—Ä–∏ –∏ –¥–æ–±—Ä–∞—Ç—å—Å—è –¥–æ —Å–µ–∫—Ü–∏–∏ D —á–µ—Ä–µ–∑ —Å–∏—Å—Ç–µ–º—É –æ–±—Ä–∞–±–æ—Ç–∫–∏ - –Ω–∞—à–µ –ø–æ–ª–æ–∂–µ–Ω–∏–µ –≤—Å–µ —Ä–∞–≤–Ω–æ –±—É–¥–µ—Ç –º—Ä–∞—á–Ω—ã–º, –Ω–æ, –ø–æ –∫—Ä–∞–π–Ω–µ–π –º–µ—Ä–µ, —ç—Ç–æ –ø–æ–º–æ–∂–µ—Ç –Ω–∞–º –≤—ã—è—Å–Ω–∏—Ç—å, –µ–¥–∏–Ω—Å—Ç–≤–µ–Ω–Ω–∞—è –ª–∏ –º—ã —Å–µ–∫—Ü–∏—è, –∫–æ—Ç–æ—Ä–∞—è –ø–æ–ø–∞–ª –≤ —Ç–∞–∫—É—é —É–∂–∞—Å–Ω—É—é —Å–∏—Ç—É–∞—Ü–∏—é.

–ï—Å–ª–∏ –ø–æ—Å–ª–µ –≤—Å–µ–≥–æ —ç—Ç–æ–≥–æ –¥–µ—Ä—å–º–∞, —è —É–∑–Ω–∞—é, —á—Ç–æ –æ—Å—Ç–∞–ª—å–Ω—ã–µ —Ç—Ä–∏ —Å–µ–∫—Ü–∏–∏ –Ω–∞ —Å–∞–º–æ–º –¥–µ–ª–µ –≤ –ø–æ–ª–Ω–æ–º –ø–æ—Ä—è–¥–∫–µ, —è –∫–æ–∂—É —Å–¥–µ—Ä—É —Å –∏—Ö —Ä—É–∫–æ–≤–æ–¥–∏—Ç–µ–ª–µ–π. –ó–∞–ø–∏—Å—å –¥–µ–Ω—å 310





–°–µ–π—á–∞—Å —è –≤ —Å–µ–∫—Ü–∏–∏ D. –†–∞–Ω—å—à–µ –∑–¥–µ—Å—å –Ω–∞—Ö–æ–¥–∏–ª—Å—è –ø–æ–ª–Ω–æ—Å—Ç—å—é –∞–≤—Ç–æ–º–∞—Ç–∏–∑–∏—Ä–æ–≤–∞–Ω–Ω—ã–π —Ü–µ–Ω—Ç—Ä –ø–æ –ø—Ä–æ–∏–∑–≤–æ–¥—Å—Ç–≤—É –ø—Ä–æ–¥—É–∫—Ç–æ–≤, –Ω–æ —Ç–µ–ø–µ—Ä—å –ø—Ä–æ–∏–∑–≤–æ–¥—Å—Ç–≤–µ–Ω–Ω–∞—è –ª–∏–Ω–∏—è –æ—Å—Ç–∞–Ω–æ–≤–ª–µ–Ω–∞. –í—Å–µ —Ä–∞–±–æ—Ç–Ω–∏–∫–∏ –∑–¥–µ—Å—å, –ø–æ—Ö–æ–∂–µ, –∏—Å—á–µ–∑–ª–∏. –ó–¥–µ—Å—å —Ü–∞—Ä–∏—Ç —Å–º–µ—Ä—Ç–µ–ª—å–Ω–∞—è —Ç–∏—à–∏–Ω–∞.

Had no one solved this apocalypse?

They had tried.

When Earth became uninhabitable, they fled underground. Subway stations. Drainage systems. Whatever kept them alive.





Survival was instinct.

Yet some resisted disaster.

If rain fell from the sky, they would reach beyond it.





The Wolke Space Station‚Äîtheir last hope.

It gathered the greatest minds. Biologists. Meteorologists. Even psychologists.





When Wolke fell, only silence remained.

A blaze so fierce, even endless rain could not quench it.

No one wept. "I, Five Clusters of Pine Needles-Mountain Gust, as a member of the Pine Needle Mountain Assembly, founder of the Noah Blanket Council, one of the Inorganic Security Maintenance Administrators, and the Sixth Duke of Deactivated Monsoon City, hereby censure all residents and assembly members of this city: Blocking the unanimous decisions of the Pine Needle Mountain Assembly directly violates the laws representing the supreme prestige of the city. Violators will be stripped of the right to ascend using the void fluid. Additionally, miniature autonomous war chariots developed by the Ninth Pillar in honor of the Sixth Pine Glory will pay a respectful visit to your hideout."





This was the looping city broadcast Nimbus heard repeatedly. Even before she gained the ability to understand language, its tonal patterns had already left a deep impression on her.

Thinking back now, perhaps the city's extinction came too swiftly; they didn‚Äôt even have the chance to shut down the broadcast.

Ironibblers covered the entire bridge. She passed far too many of them. Or was it improper to use the term "same kind" for inorganic beings? They gnawed at the bridge. She believed they were also devouring the supports beneath Deactivated Monsoon, though she couldn‚Äôt comprehend why that troubled him.

Beneath the mountains, there should have been dry ground. A fall from such a height would be fatal. But the accelerated rain cycles had turned below into a sea wedged between towering peaks.

Before receiving the Mark of Communication, Deactivated Monsoon had done something to her. He dismantled parts of his own body for an operation she didn‚Äôt understand. She could only assume it was well-intentioned‚Äîshe couldn‚Äôt imagine Monsoon doing harm to her.





"Do you see that communication tower towering above all others? Yes, the one at the edge of the clouds. That is your destination."

That was her destination.

Nimbus had walked the bridge for too long. Another rain cycle loomed, with raindrops starting to strike her body. Things would soon turn dire. Never mind whether the rain would rise high enough to drown her; the sheer weight of the deluge could wash her away.

The nearest peak seemed impossibly far from Monsoon's superstructure. Worse still, she had no sense of how much of the journey remained. Perhaps she hadn‚Äôt even covered a tenth‚Äîor a thousandth‚Äîof it. What kind of impossible mission had her creator entrusted to her?

And yet, she wanted to fulfill it. She had to.

So she kept moving.





Until the bridge tilted beneath her feet, until the path before her was no longer flat, until she lost her balance and slipped from the collapsing bridge into the sea between the mountains. I remember little of Deactivated Monsoon. He cared too much for native and companion creatures. When irrationality spread among our kind, some acted unethically.

They perished shortly after the void fluid revolution. Few escaped, and none sought refuge in my city.

Did Nimbus return to Monsoon‚Äôs land? I do not know. I can only guess.





Through rain-drenched mountains, she pressed on. But without rain, she moved slowly.

When dark clouds gathered, a biting wind howled.

There was no sign of Monsoon‚Äôs structure‚Äîonly snow.

Snow? She had no word for it. She only felt the sting of cold.

Flakes of white fell endlessly.

The familiar landscape had changed. Monsoon‚Äôs structure was a wreck. Ironibblers had vanished. Nothing lived.

Only Nimbus.





Forward. Keep moving.





For an impossible goal.





For materialism.





She could no longer ascend.

Before the end, the world had already decided hers, so long ago.





Wind and snow. And a shadow.

They stood. Watched.

Were they kin? Predator? It didn‚Äôt matter.

For one who would never ascend, nothing mattered.





The shadow bore witness to her silent, frozen end. The rain intensified. Time was running out‚Äîfor Nimbus and her adversaries alike.

Sensing the impending rain, most of the lizards and salamanders conceded defeat and retreated into the cracks of the ground. Only two blue ones remained‚Äîstill locked in combat with the king vulture.

With a violent twist, the vulture tossed one of the blue lizards into a distant trash heap.

Nimbus made her choice. Without hesitation, she flung her spear at the king vulture‚Äôs head, shattering its grotesque mask. Perhaps it was the rain, or perhaps it was finally injured‚Äîthe vulture took flight, leaving the battlefield.

The surviving blue lizard and Nimbus exchanged glances.

In this storm, neither of them had a chance. Both would perish under the rain.

Would she loop here?

The lizard made a gurgling sound and turned away.

Nimbus sprinted to retrieve the fallen mask and raced toward the nearest shelter.

The rain poured relentlessly.

She stumbled, overwhelmed by the deluge, unable to rise.

This should have been the end.





In the rain. In the downpour.

Nimbus stood.

She overcame the rain.

No‚Äîshe had never possessed such an ability before. How‚Ä¶ How could she walk in the rain?

Riding the rain‚Ä¶? Why?

She could never have guessed‚Äîthis was the genetic modification Deactivated Monsoon had performed. She only knew she no longer feared the storm.

Steam burst from her body, evaporating the rain in fierce clouds. Propelled by the pressure, she ascended like a vulture. Her small, slugcat frame made her nimble, immune to the crushing force of the rain.

Upward.

That was her new goal.

For in the rain, even with movement, nothing else could be achieved.





Soon, Nimbus rose above the storm. Higher than the dark clouds.

Finally, she reached a place where torrential rain would never fall. Drip. A raindrop struck the tip of her spear, scattering into mist. With a sharp whoosh, the spear, aimed at the salamander‚Äôs head, bounced harmlessly away.

Their skulls were far too hard.

Nimbus knew better than to charge back into the fray to retrieve her spear. Instead, she grabbed a nearby rock and hurled it at the blue lizard. It stumbled, but kept advancing, unfazed by the barrage of stones and debris.





Drip. Another raindrop.

Desperately searching for a better weapon, she scrambled backward until her hand closed around a squishy, cocoon-like creature. Without thinking, she flung it at the approaching lizard. The salamander bit down, and to Nimbus's astonishment, a yellow laser shot out, turning green in midair.

A giant green lizard lunged to snatch the prize, locking jaws with its blue counterpart. In a flash, it ripped its adversary‚Äôs throat out.

But more lizards‚Äîgreen, blue, and pink‚Äîwere already closing in on Nimbus.





Rain began to fall harder. For a moment, the downpour relented, replaced by an ominous red beam.

Nimbus knew the source. Flying‚Ä¶ masked‚Ä¶ the vultures.

A curved, massive lance descended from above, impaling an unlucky blue lizard. The king vulture‚Äôs hissing jets grew louder as terrified green lizards fled. The blue and pink ones, stunned, soon rallied to attack.

Nimbus gripped a new spear but hesitated. Which target? The blue lizard? Or the vulture, impervious to mere spears?

She raised her eyes. The storm clouds churned dark and heavy.

Another cycle was about to end. She had no idea how so many scavengers had gathered in this place.

Nimbus had been parkouring across the outer walls for what felt like an eternity, yet scavengers kept appearing from pipes and crevices. Why were they all targeting her? What had she done?

Then it hit her‚Äîthe golden pearl she carried.

No. This pearl isn‚Äôt for you!

She didn‚Äôt want to attack them, so all she could do was run.

Finally, she reached the top of the superstructure. A vast, desolate city lay before her, cloaked in dust. Nimbus trudged forward, dodging spears that barely missed her. Her patience snapped. She grabbed a loose object and hurled it back.

An explosion.

Scavengers tumbled away. To her horror, she realized it had been a bomb.

With a pang of guilt, she threw another of it at the next group blocking her way.

When the smoke cleared, the path lay open. Scavengers writhed on the ground.

She sighed in relief, wishing she‚Äôd brought the king vulture‚Äôs mask‚Äîbut dragging it had made flight impossible.





Navigating the interior of the structure was surprisingly straightforward. Nimbus, a veteran of Monsoon‚Äôs labyrinthine layout, reached the chamber of the structure‚Äôs master.

"Ah, you‚Äôve arrived‚Ä¶ I‚Äôve been watching, little one. That Mark of Communication‚Äîyou received it from an old friend of mine."

She understood the words of the Iterator marked with the sun. But she could not reply.

"I wondered if I should send help‚Ä¶ but it seems you‚Äôve managed on your own," the Iterator spoke gently. "And‚Ä¶ you‚Äôve brought me something."

Nimbus spat out the golden pearl. Crackling energy lifted it into the air. Analysis screens flared to life.

Then Seven Red Suns recoiled in shock.

"Monsoon‚Ä¶ is this truly what you concluded‚Ä¶ in your final moments?"

He calmed himself before addressing Nimbus. "This message should not have reached me, but I will handle it. You‚Äôve done well."

He descended, placing a careful hand on her head.

"I am Seven Red Suns. Monsoon was my friend. That pearl you had carries troubling revelations, but I will find a way forward."

Nimbus listened, though the exchange ended abruptly.

"Are you in a hurry to return?"

She stood still.

"I can‚Äôt receive Monsoon‚Äôs signal anymore. Returning may be dangerous. Are you sure?"

She had no choice. She couldn‚Äôt answer.

"Thank you for the pearl. One last thing‚Äîmay I scan your genetic makeup? Monsoon‚Ä¶ altered you in ways I‚Äôd like to understand."

This became the second gift she left for Seven Red Suns.





As she departed through a pipe, he murmured to himself, gazing at the pearl.

"Desire and ignorance aren‚Äôt frightening‚Ä¶ but Monsoon, you feared death more than anyone. That third primal sin has ensnared your messenger."

He stared into the golden pearl.

"Does this tell‚Ä¶ how an Iterator ends itself?" She was washed ashore on unfamiliar terrain, the farthest point she had ever traveled. She never imagined reaching such a distant place.

The first problem was that she still had no idea how much further lay ahead. The communication tower was barely visible on the horizon‚Äîan unreachable speck.

The second problem was that there were no more mountains. She had been swept into a wholly foreign domain, unsure if her journey had lengthened.

Swimming across the ocean to reach the tower? Not a good plan. So she lingered along the shoreline, scavenging for food and finding shelter, where she slept through 3 rain cycles. She didn‚Äôt understand why, but when she approached a massive metal gate she had seen in earlier cycles, it suddenly roared to life.

When the gate opened, she realized she had a new path‚Äîone that didn‚Äôt involve swimming only to be swept ashore again. She could take the long way around.

It was only when she encountered exotic, dangerous lizards on this seemingly safer route that she realized it would be no simple journey.

Green ones? Blue ones? Even rare pink salamanders that could swim? Any of them would be deadly.

One mistake would be fatal. So she picked up a discarded spear.

A battle was about to begin. On the steel islands, golden and orange hues bathed the skies, and strange, wondrous creatures roamed.

A squid-like white flyer hovered nearby, curious about the dazed Nimbus. Soon, more white and even black squidcadas gathered, the buzzing of their wings a chorus of sound. In the distance, a green-winged centipede spun aimlessly in the open air.

Freed from the rain, Nimbus could no longer fly. But she wasn‚Äôt worried. Crossing a few more sky islands would bring her to her destination.

She could see it‚Äîjust beyond reach‚Äîa massive structure belonging to a Random God. Other superstructures lay too far for her to grasp. This one would be her end point.

And so, she hugged the squidcada.

Traversing the sky islands didn‚Äôt take long. Blue lizards chased her briefly, but soon turned on closer prey. Their camaraderie amused her.

Finally, she climbed the towering wall of the superstructure, releasing the exhausted squidcada. She caught some batflies for her newfound friend. They feasted together.

Parting ways, Nimbus entered the towering gateway. Beyond lay darkness.

On the walls she passed, two ancient figures faced each other, seated in reverence. The graffiti‚Äôs meaning was lost on her.

She was merely a messenger. She had come to fulfill Deactivated Monsoon‚Äôs dying wish.

The rest was forgotten.





A few red overseers had long signaled that Nimbus had entered the wrong place, but their presence also meant she had attracted the attention of this god.

As she navigated the structure's dark halls, a few twists and turns revealed flickering lights.

No, it wasn‚Äôt fire. Under the blue illuminations, a bustling marketplace stretched before her, illuminating the gloom.

She suddenly realized this superstructure had been claimed by some sort of residents. Intelligent beings had infiltrated it, bypassing its defensive systems. The weapons they clutched confirmed her suspicions.

And worse, they were hostile.

Realizing this, Nimbus turned and fled.

The monkey-like figures brandished their weapons and chased after her.

Scavengers.
